Procedure after Aneen's Claim of Consummation
Procedure for resolving conflicting claims after respite for impotence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure when an aneen husband claims consummation after his year, and apply the rules of physical inspection and oath to determine the wife's option.

Core Idea
The wife's option after the aneen's respite hinges on either virginity found by inspection or the husband's refusal to swear.

When an impotent husband (aneen) is granted a one-year respite, a common dispute arises if he later claims he has consummated the marriage while the wife denies. This passage from Al-Hidayah details the qadi's procedural steps to resolve the conflict. The ruling balances the need for evidence (physical or oath-based) to protect the wife from being trapped in a defective marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting claims
The husband asserts consummation after the year; the wife denies it. This creates a dispute requiring judicial resolution.
The respite is already granted, so the issue is whether the husband is now capable.
2
Order physical inspection by women
The qadi appoints female examiners (usually relatives or midwives) to inspect the wife's physical state to determine virginity (bikr) or non-virginity (thayyib).
This is a form of shahadat al-nisa', accepted in matters men cannot access.
3
Interpret the inspection result
If the women declare she is still a virgin, this corroborates the wife's denial, and she is immediately given the option (khiyar) to stay or seek separation. If they declare her thayyib, the case moves to the next step.
Virginity is a 'supporter' (mu'ayyid) for the wife's claim. Thayyib means the husband's claim is plausible.
4
Require the husband's oath if thayyib
The qadi asks the husband to swear an oath that he did consummate the marriage. If he swears, his claim is upheld and the wife loses the option. If he refuses (nukul), the refusal supports the wife, and she is given the option.
Refusal to take an oath is treated as evidence against the husband.
5
Conclude the option
The wife's khiyar is granted if either inspection finds virginity or the husband refuses the oath. If the husband swears, she has no option and the marriage continues.
The procedure ensures that false claims are deterred by physical evidence or oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و اذا اجل العنين سنة وقال قدجامعتها وانكرت نظر اليها النساء فان قلن هى بكر خيرت لان شهادتهن تأيدت بمؤيد و هي البكارة و ان قلن هى ثيب حلف الزوج فان نكل خيرت لتأيدها بالنكول وان حلف لا يخير
And when the impotent man (aneen) is given a respite of one year and he says, 'I have had intercourse with her,' and she denies, then women look at her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), she is given the choice (khiyar), because their testimony is supported by a supporter, which is virginity. And if they say she is thayyib, the husband takes an oath, and if he refuses, she is given the choice, because she is supported by his refusal. And if he takes an oath, she is not given the choice.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage details the procedure after an impotent husband ('aneen) has been given a one-year respite as previously prescribed. After the year, if the husband claims that he has now consummated the marriage, and the wife denies this, the qadi must investigate. Women (usually female relatives or midwives) are appointed to inspect the wife. Their finding determines the next step: If they find her still a virgin (bikr), this corroborates the wife's denial and disproves the husband's claim. In this case, the wife is given the option (khiyar) to either stay in the marriage or seek separation (faskh). The reason given is that the women's testimony is supported by a 'supporter' (mu'ayyid) – namely, the intact hymen. If the women find her no longer a virgin (thayyib), the matter becomes murkier because the loss of virginity could be due to the husband or other causes. Then the husband is asked to take an oath that he did consummate. If he takes the oath, his claim is upheld and the wife has no option. If he refuses to swear (nukul), this refusal is taken as a sign supporting the wife's claim, and she is given the option. The commentary notes that the inspection happens twice: once before granting the respite (to establish the initial state) and once after the year (to determine the outcome).

Key Terms
خيرت (khuyyirat or khayyir): She is given the choice (option) to either stay married or seek separation.
نكل (nakala / nukul): Refusal to take the oath after being asked; such refusal may be deemed as evidence against the refuser.
شهادة النّساء (shahadat al-nisa'): The testimony of women inspecting the wife's physical state; in this context, their testimony is accepted as evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After a one-year respite for an aneen husband who claims consummation while the wife denies, what happens if the inspecting women find the wife is thayyib?
A) The wife gets an option immediately
B) The husband is given an additional year
C) The husband takes an oath; if he refuses, the wife gets option
D) The marriage is annulled immediately

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to khiyar after the aneen's respite hinges on either physical evidence of virginity or the husband's refusal to take an oath.

Types of Male Deficiency and Their Rulings
Hanafi classification and ruling for three types of male deficiency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the ‘aneen, majbub, and khasiyy and state the Hanafi ruling regarding immediate separation or granting a one-year respite.

Core Idea
Majbub gets no hope; ‘aneen and khasiyy get a year’s chance.

Hanafi law treats different forms of male sexual deficiency with distinct rulings. A husband whose penis is removed (majbub) cannot be cured, so separation is immediate upon the wife’s request. But an impotent man (‘aneen) who still has the organ, and a castrated man (khasiyy) who retains the organ, are given a full lunar year to attempt intercourse, because cure is still possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Name the three terms: ‘aneen (impotent), majbub (penis removed), khasiyy (testicles removed). State the distinguishing feature for each.
2
State the ruling for each
For the majbub: immediate separation if wife demands. For the ‘aneen and khasiyy: one-year respite before separation can be considered.
3
Explain the rationale
The majbub has no organ left, so hope of intercourse is zero. The other two still have the organ, so a chance of cure exists.

اگر عورت پہلے سے شیبہ ہے مرد کا قول قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہوگا
و ان كان ثيبافي الاصل فالقول قوله مع يمينه وقد ذكرناه فان اختارت زوجها لم يكن لها بعد ذالك خيار لانها رضيت ببطلان حقها وفى التاجيل تعتبر السنة القمرية هو الصحيح ويحتسب بايام الحيض وبشهر رمضان لوجود ذالك فى السنة ولا يحتسب بمرضه ومرضها لان السنة قد تخلو عنه
ترجمہ اور اگر یہ عورت پہلے سے ثیبہ ہوتو شوہر کا قول قسم کے ساتھ قبول ہوگا اور ہم اس کو پہلے ذکر کر چکے ۔ پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر کو اختیار کر لیا تو اس کو اس کے بعد خیار نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی ہے اور مہلت کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یہی صحیح قول ہے اور ایام حیض اور رمضان کا مہینہ بھی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سال میں ان کا وجود ضروری ہے اور مرد کی بیماری اور عورت کی بیماری ( کے ایام ) شمار نہیں ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ سال کبھی بیماری سے خالی ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت پہلے سے ہی ثیبہ تھی تو اس کے شوہر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ شوہر استحقاق فرقت کا منکر ہے اور عورت مدعیہ ہے اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے جب کہ بعینہ نہ ہو پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شو ہر کو اختیار کر لیا یعنی نامرد ہونے کے باوجود اس کے ساتھ رہنا منظور کر لیا تو اس کے بعد بیوی کو تفریق کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت بذات خود اپنا حق باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نا مرد کو مہلت دینے کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۵۴ یوم اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شمسی سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۶۵ دن پورے اور ایک دن کا چوتھائی اور ایک دن کا ایک سو بیسواں حصہ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور ایک سال کی مدت میں حیض کے دن اور رمضان المبارک کا مہینہ منہا نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ سال کی مدت میں یہ ایام بھی محصوب. ناوں گے کیونکہ سال کے دوران ان ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ البتہ شوہر کی بیماری کے ایام اور عورت کی بیماری کے ایام منہا ہوں گے۔ سال کی مدت میں ان ایام کو شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بیماری کے ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بسا اوقات سال کی مدت بیماری سے خالی ہوتی ہے۔
Chapter of the Impotent and Others. The woman will have no right, and if he refuses to take an oath, he will be given a respite of one year. As for how it will be known whether the woman is a thayyib or a bikr, the author of al-‘Inayah has mentioned three ways. First, a small egg of a hen is inserted into the woman’s private part; if it goes in easily without difficulty, she is a thayyib, otherwise a bikr. Second, if it is possible for the woman to urinate against a wall, she is a bikr, otherwise a thayyib. Third, an egg is broken and its contents poured into the woman’s private part; if it goes inside, then she is a thayyib, otherwise a bikr. And Allah knows best. If the husband is a majbub (one whose penis is cut off), the judge will immediately separate them if the woman demands, because there is no benefit in giving a respite. And the khasiyy (castrated man) will be given a respite just as the ‘aneen is given a respite, because his intercourse is hoped for. Translation: And if the husband is maqtū‘ al-dhakar (penis cut off), then immediate separation will be made between the two provided the woman requests. Because there is no benefit in granting a respite. And the khasiyy will also be given a respite like the ‘aneen, because intercourse is hoped from him. Explanation: The issue is that if the husband is maqtū‘ al-dhakar, then separation is made without respite, provided the woman requests separation. Because from the side of the maqtū‘ al-dhakar, no wali (healing) is expected. Therefore, there is no benefit in granting him a respite. And the ākhta (one whose testicles have been removed) will also be given a respite like the impotent man, because intercourse is hoped from him too. That is, the penis exists, perhaps at some time the power of intercourse may develop in it. When the ‘aneen is given a respite of one year and he says, “I had intercourse with her,” and the woman denies, women are made to examine her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), then she is given the choice (khiyār), because their testimony is strengthened by the supporting evidence (mu’ayyid) which is virginity. And if they say she is a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. If he refuses, she is given the choice because of her being strengthened by his refusal. And if he takes the oath, she is given no choice. Translation: And when the ‘aneen is given a respite of one year and he says, “I had intercourse with her,” and she denies, women look at her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), then she is given the choice. Because the testimony of the women is strengthened by the supporting evidence, which is virginity. And if they say she is a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. Then if he refuses, the woman is given the choice because of her being strengthened by his refusal. And if he takes the oath, the woman is not given the choice. Explanation: The scenario is that if the judge gave the ‘aneen a respite of one year. Then he said, “I had intercourse within the year,” and the woman denies intercourse, then women look at her. This looking by women occurs twice: once before granting respite and once after the period has passed. In any case, if after the respite period, the women see and say that the woman is still a virgin, the judge will give her the choice. Then if she chooses separation, the judge will separate them. The proof is that the women’s testimony is strengthened by her being a virgin; therefore, the man’s claim that he has had intercourse is false. And if the women see and say she has become a thayyib, then the husband is made to take an oath. Then if the husband refuses to take an oath, the woman is also given the choice, because the woman’s claim (that he has not had intercourse) is strengthened by the husband’s refusal to swear. And if the husband takes the oath, the woman will not have the choice, because the women’s testimony and the husband’s oath have nullified her right. If the woman was previously a thayyib, then the man’s statement along with his oath will be accepted. And we have mentioned this before. So if the woman chooses her husband, thereafter she has no choice, because she has consented to the nullification of her right. And regarding the respite, the lunar year is considered; this is the correct view. And the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted (within the year), because they necessarily occur in a year. And his illness and her illness are not counted, because a year may be free from illness. Translation: And if this woman had been a thayyib originally, then the husband’s statement along with his oath will be accepted, and we have mentioned this before. So if the woman chooses her husband, thereafter she has no choice, because she has consented to the nullification of her right. And in the respite, the lunar year is considered; this is the correct view. And the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted, because their occurrence in a year is necessary. And the husband’s illness and the wife’s illness are not counted, because a year may be free from illness. Explanation: The issue is that if the woman was originally a thayyib, then her husband’s statement with an oath is accepted. The reason has passed earlier that the husband is the denier (munkir) of deserving separation and the woman is the claimant (mudda‘iyah), and the statement of the denier is accepted when there is no evidence. So if the woman chose her husband, meaning she accepted to remain with him despite his impotence, then afterwards the wife will have no right to demand separation, because she has herself consented to nullify her right. The author of Hidāyah says that in the period of respite for the impotent man, the lunar year is considered, i.e., 354 days. And there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah that the solar year is considered, i.e., 365 days, a quarter, and one hundred twentieth of a day. And in the duration of one year, the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan will not be subtracted; rather these days will also be counted in the year, because the occurrence of these days during the year is necessary. But the days of the husband’s illness and the wife’s illness will be subtracted; these days will not be counted in the year’s duration, because the occurrence of illness is not necessary; rather sometimes the year’s duration is free from illness.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with rulings related to a husband who is impotent (‘aneen) or castrated (majbub/khasiyy). It begins by stating that if a husband refuses to take an oath regarding impotency, he is given a one-year respite. The author then discusses methods to determine whether a woman is a virgin (bikr) or non-virgin (thayyib) as cited from al-‘Inayah, including inserting a hen’s egg, urinating against a wall, or pouring egg white into the private part. While these methods are mentioned, they are not part of the core legal ruling but are practical indicators.

The core ruling: If the husband is majbub (penis removed), the judge immediately separates them upon the wife’s request because there is no hope of cure. If he is khasiyy (testicles removed) or ākhta, a respite is given like the ‘aneen because intercourse is still possible. For the ‘aneen, after a one-year respite, if the husband claims he had intercourse but the wife denies, women inspect her. If they find her still a virgin, the wife is given the choice to separate or stay, as the women’s testimony is strengthened by the physical sign. If they find her a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. If he refuses, she gets the choice; if he swears, she loses the right to separation.

If the woman was already a thayyib before the respite, the husband’s denial of failure to have intercourse is accepted with his oath. If the wife chooses to stay with him, she cannot later demand separation.

Regarding the calculation of the one-year respite, the correct view (al-sahih) is that it is a lunar year (354 days). A narration from Abu Hanifah says solar year (365.25 days), but the relied-upon position is lunar. Days of menstruation and Ramadan are counted within the year because they necessarily occur. Days of illness for either spouse are not counted, because illness is not guaranteed to occur, so the year is calculated based on healthy days.

Key Terms
عنين ('aneen): A man who is impotent and unable to perform intercourse due to an organic or psychological condition.
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis has been cut off (maqtū‘ al-dhakar).
خصي (khaṣiyy): A man whose testicles have been removed (castrated).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which husband is separated from his wife immediately upon her request?
A) The 'aneen (impotent)
B) The majbub (penis removed)
C) The khasiyy (testicles removed)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
A majbub is separated immediately, while an 'aneen and khasiyy get a one-year respite because the organ of intercourse is still present.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Evidence Procedure After the Respite: Virginity Test and Oaths
Hanafi procedure for resolving dispute over consummation after the respite period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the procedure when an ‘aneen claims he had intercourse after the respite, including the women's examination, the role of virginity, the husband's oath, and the wife's khiyar.

Core Idea
The wife’s physical state after a year decides the dispute: if still a virgin, she has full choice; if not, the husband’s oath prevails.

When an impotent husband claims he succeeded after the year, the law does not take his word alone. Women inspect the wife. If she remains a virgin, her claim is strengthened and she gets the option to separate. If she has lost virginity, the husband swears an oath and she loses the right. A special rule applies if she was already a thayyib before marriage.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
After the one-year respite, the ‘aneen claims he had intercourse. The wife denies it. The judge appoints women to examine her.
2
Two possible outcomes from examination
If the women find her still a virgin (bikr), her testimony is strengthened, and she is given khiyar (choice to separate or stay). If they find her a thayyib (non-virgin), the husband is made to take an oath that he did have intercourse; if he swears, she loses the khiyar; if he refuses to swear, she gets the khiyar.
3
Rule for a woman originally thayyib
If she was already a thayyib at the time of marriage, the virginity test is not useful. Instead, the husband’s statement (with oath) that he did have intercourse is accepted as the default. But if she later chooses to stay with him, she cannot afterwards demand separation based on his impotence.

جب عنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی اور اس نے کہا میں نے جماع کیا عورت انکار کرتی ہے قاضی عورتوں سے معائنہ کروائے اگر وہ باکرہ کہہ دیں تو اسے اختیار دے دیا جائے اگر وہ شیبہ کہ دیں زوج قسم اٹھائے
و اذا اجل العنين سنة وقال قدجامعتها وانكرت نظر اليها النساء فان قلن هي بكر خيرت لان شهادتهن تأيدت بمؤيد و هي البكارة و ان قلن هي ثيب حلف الزوج فان نكل خيرت لتأيدها بالنكول وان حلف لا يخير ترجمه . اور جب عنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی گئی اور کہا اس نے کہ میں نے اس عورت سے جماع کر لیا ہے اور اس عورت نے انکار کیا تو اس کو عورتیں دیکھیں پس اگر عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ باکرہ موجود ہے۔ تو عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عورتوں کی گواہی ،موید یعنی باکرہ ہونے سے قوی ہوگئی اور اگر عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ شیبہ ہوگئی ہے تو شوہر سے قسم لی جائے گی پس اگر اس نے انکار کیا تو عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ شوہر کے انکار سے اس کی تائید ہوگئی اور اگر قسم کھا گیا تو عورت مختار نہ ہو گی۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاکم نے حسنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی۔ پھر اس نے کہا میں نے ایک سال کے اندر اندر جماع کر لیا اور عورت جماع کی منکر ہے تو اس کو عورت دیکھیں عورتوں کا یہ دیکھنا دو مرتبہ ہو گا ایک مرتبہ مہلت دینے سے پہلے اور ایک مرتبہ مدت گزرجانے کے بعد بہر حال اگر عورتوں نے مدت تاجیل کے بعد دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ عورت ابھی بھی باکرہ ہے تو قاضی اس عورت کو اختیار دے گا۔ پس اگر اس نے فرقت کو ترجیح دی تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اس کے باکرہ ہونے سے قوی ہوگئی ہے اس وجہ سے مرد کا یہ کہنا کہ میں جماع کر چکا ہوں غلط ہے۔ اور اگر ان عورتوں نے دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ تو شیبہ ہوگئی ہے تو شوہر سے قسم لی جائے گی پس اگر شوہر نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو بھی عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ شوہر کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دینے کی وجہ سے عورت کے دعوئی ( کہ مجھ سے جماع نہیں کیا ) کی تائید ہوگئی ہے اور اگر شو ہر قسم کھا گیا تو عورت کو اختیار نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اور شوہر کے قسم کھانے سے اس کا حق باطل ہو چکا ہے۔
اگر عورت پہلے سے شیبہ ہے مرد کا قول قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہوگا
و ان كان ثيبافي الاصل فالقول قوله مع يمينه وقد ذكرناه فان اختارت زوجها لم يكن لها بعد ذالك خيار لانها رضيت ببطلان حقها وفى التاجيل تعتبر السنة القمرية هو الصحيح ويحتسب بايام الحيض وبشهر رمضان لوجود ذالك فى السنة ولا يحتسب بمرضه ومرضها لان السنة قد تخلو عنه
ترجمہ اور اگر یہ عورت پہلے سے ثیبہ ہوتو شوہر کا قول قسم کے ساتھ قبول ہوگا اور ہم اس کو پہلے ذکر کر چکے ۔ پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر کو اختیار کر لیا تو اس کو اس کے بعد خیار نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی ہے اور مہلت کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یہی صحیح قول ہے اور ایام حیض اور رمضان کا مہینہ بھی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سال میں ان کا وجود ضروری ہے اور مرد کی بیماری اور عورت کی بیماری ( کے ایام ) شمار نہیں ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ سال کبھی بیماری سے خالی ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت پہلے سے ہی ثیبہ تھی تو اس کے شوہر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ شوہر استحقاق فرقت کا منکر ہے اور عورت مدعیہ ہے اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے جب کہ بعینہ نہ ہو پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شو ہر کو اختیار کر لیا یعنی نامرد ہونے کے باوجود اس کے ساتھ رہنا منظور کر لیا تو اس کے بعد بیوی کو تفریق کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت بذات خود اپنا حق باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نا مرد کو مہلت دینے کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۵۴ یوم اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شمسی سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۶۵ دن پورے اور ایک دن کا چوتھائی اور ایک دن کا ایک سو بیسواں حصہ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور ایک سال کی مدت میں حیض کے دن اور رمضان المبارک کا مہینہ منہا نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ سال کی مدت میں یہ ایام بھی محصوب. ناوں گے کیونکہ سال کے دوران ان ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ البتہ شوہر کی بیماری کے ایام اور عورت کی بیماری کے ایام منہا ہوں گے۔ سال کی مدت میں ان ایام کو شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بیماری کے ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بسا اوقات سال کی مدت بیماری سے خالی ہوتی ہے۔
Chapter of the Impotent and Others. The woman will have no right, and if he refuses to take an oath, he will be given a respite of one year. As for how it will be known whether the woman is a thayyib or a bikr, the author of al-‘Inayah has mentioned three ways. First, a small egg of a hen is inserted into the woman’s private part; if it goes in easily without difficulty, she is a thayyib, otherwise a bikr. Second, if it is possible for the woman to urinate against a wall, she is a bikr, otherwise a thayyib. Third, an egg is broken and its contents poured into the woman’s private part; if it goes inside, then she is a thayyib, otherwise a bikr. And Allah knows best. If the husband is a majbub (one whose penis is cut off), the judge will immediately separate them if the woman demands, because there is no benefit in giving a respite. And the khasiyy (castrated man) will be given a respite just as the ‘aneen is given a respite, because his intercourse is hoped for. Translation: And if the husband is maqtū‘ al-dhakar (penis cut off), then immediate separation will be made between the two provided the woman requests. Because there is no benefit in granting a respite. And the khasiyy will also be given a respite like the ‘aneen, because intercourse is hoped from him. Explanation: The issue is that if the husband is maqtū‘ al-dhakar, then separation is made without respite, provided the woman requests separation. Because from the side of the maqtū‘ al-dhakar, no wali (healing) is expected. Therefore, there is no benefit in granting him a respite. And the ākhta (one whose testicles have been removed) will also be given a respite like the impotent man, because intercourse is hoped from him too. That is, the penis exists, perhaps at some time the power of intercourse may develop in it. When the ‘aneen is given a respite of one year and he says, “I had intercourse with her,” and the woman denies, women are made to examine her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), then she is given the choice (khiyār), because their testimony is strengthened by the supporting evidence (mu’ayyid) which is virginity. And if they say she is a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. If he refuses, she is given the choice because of her being strengthened by his refusal. And if he takes the oath, she is given no choice. Translation: And when the ‘aneen is given a respite of one year and he says, “I had intercourse with her,” and she denies, women look at her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), then she is given the choice. Because the testimony of the women is strengthened by the supporting evidence, which is virginity. And if they say she is a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. Then if he refuses, the woman is given the choice because of her being strengthened by his refusal. And if he takes the oath, the woman is not given the choice. Explanation: The scenario is that if the judge gave the ‘aneen a respite of one year. Then he said, “I had intercourse within the year,” and the woman denies intercourse, then women look at her. This looking by women occurs twice: once before granting respite and once after the period has passed. In any case, if after the respite period, the women see and say that the woman is still a virgin, the judge will give her the choice. Then if she chooses separation, the judge will separate them. The proof is that the women’s testimony is strengthened by her being a virgin; therefore, the man’s claim that he has had intercourse is false. And if the women see and say she has become a thayyib, then the husband is made to take an oath. Then if the husband refuses to take an oath, the woman is also given the choice, because the woman’s claim (that he has not had intercourse) is strengthened by the husband’s refusal to swear. And if the husband takes the oath, the woman will not have the choice, because the women’s testimony and the husband’s oath have nullified her right. If the woman was previously a thayyib, then the man’s statement along with his oath will be accepted. And we have mentioned this before. So if the woman chooses her husband, thereafter she has no choice, because she has consented to the nullification of her right. And regarding the respite, the lunar year is considered; this is the correct view. And the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted (within the year), because they necessarily occur in a year. And his illness and her illness are not counted, because a year may be free from illness. Translation: And if this woman had been a thayyib originally, then the husband’s statement along with his oath will be accepted, and we have mentioned this before. So if the woman chooses her husband, thereafter she has no choice, because she has consented to the nullification of her right. And in the respite, the lunar year is considered; this is the correct view. And the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted, because their occurrence in a year is necessary. And the husband’s illness and the wife’s illness are not counted, because a year may be free from illness. Explanation: The issue is that if the woman was originally a thayyib, then her husband’s statement with an oath is accepted. The reason has passed earlier that the husband is the denier (munkir) of deserving separation and the woman is the claimant (mudda‘iyah), and the statement of the denier is accepted when there is no evidence. So if the woman chose her husband, meaning she accepted to remain with him despite his impotence, then afterwards the wife will have no right to demand separation, because she has herself consented to nullify her right. The author of Hidāyah says that in the period of respite for the impotent man, the lunar year is considered, i.e., 354 days. And there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah that the solar year is considered, i.e., 365 days, a quarter, and one hundred twentieth of a day. And in the duration of one year, the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan will not be subtracted; rather these days will also be counted in the year, because the occurrence of these days during the year is necessary. But the days of the husband’s illness and the wife’s illness will be subtracted; these days will not be counted in the year’s duration, because the occurrence of illness is not necessary; rather sometimes the year’s duration is free from illness.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with rulings related to a husband who is impotent (‘aneen) or castrated (majbub/khasiyy). It begins by stating that if a husband refuses to take an oath regarding impotency, he is given a one-year respite. The author then discusses methods to determine whether a woman is a virgin (bikr) or non-virgin (thayyib) as cited from al-‘Inayah, including inserting a hen’s egg, urinating against a wall, or pouring egg white into the private part. While these methods are mentioned, they are not part of the core legal ruling but are practical indicators.

The core ruling: If the husband is majbub (penis removed), the judge immediately separates them upon the wife’s request because there is no hope of cure. If he is khasiyy (testicles removed) or ākhta, a respite is given like the ‘aneen because intercourse is still possible. For the ‘aneen, after a one-year respite, if the husband claims he had intercourse but the wife denies, women inspect her. If they find her still a virgin, the wife is given the choice to separate or stay, as the women’s testimony is strengthened by the physical sign. If they find her a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. If he refuses, she gets the choice; if he swears, she loses the right to separation.

If the woman was already a thayyib before the respite, the husband’s denial of failure to have intercourse is accepted with his oath. If the wife chooses to stay with him, she cannot later demand separation.

Regarding the calculation of the one-year respite, the correct view (al-sahih) is that it is a lunar year (354 days). A narration from Abu Hanifah says solar year (365.25 days), but the relied-upon position is lunar. Days of menstruation and Ramadan are counted within the year because they necessarily occur. Days of illness for either spouse are not counted, because illness is not guaranteed to occur, so the year is calculated based on healthy days.

Key Terms
بكر (bikr): A virgin woman with intact hymen.
ثيب (thayyib): A non-virgin woman who has had intercourse.
خيار (khiyar): The wife's option to annul the marriage or continue.
نكول (nukūl): Refusal to take an oath after being required to do so.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After the respite, the husband claims intercourse, wife denies. Women examine her and find her a thayyib. The husband is asked to swear an oath that he did have intercourse. He refuses. What is the ruling?
A) The wife loses her right to separation.
B) The wife gets the choice to separate or stay.
C) The judge forces the husband to divorce.
D) The case is dismissed.

Key Takeaway
The wife's prior virginity or its loss determines the evidence procedure; if she was originally a thayyib, the husband's oath settles the matter.

Nikah — Marriage

Calculating the One-Year Respite: Lunar Year and Exclusion of Illness
Hanafi calculation of the respite period, including the ikhtilaf on lunar vs solar year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the one-year respite for the ‘aneen as a lunar year of 354 days, counting days of menstruation and Ramadan but excluding days of illness, and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between lunar and solar year.

Core Idea
The respite is a lunar year of 354 days; illness of either spouse is not counted because it is not inevitable.

The one-year respite is not arbitrary: it follows the Islamic lunar calendar. All days count, including menstruation and Ramadan, because these occur in every year. But if the husband or wife becomes ill during the year, those days are subtracted, because illness is not guaranteed. An alternative view from Imam Abu Hanifah opts for the solar year, but the relied-upon view is lunar.

Guided Path
1
Determine the default year type
The correct (sahih) view is that the year is a lunar year of approximately 354 days. Understand the evidence: Islamic legal periods (iddah, etc.) are based on lunar months.
2
What days are counted?
Days of menstruation (hayd) and the month of Ramadan are counted within the year because they inevitably occur. The fact that intercourse may not be possible during these days does not exclude them.
3
What days are excluded?
Days when either the husband or the wife suffers an illness (marad) are not counted. Because a year can pass without illness; it is not a constant factor.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf
A narration from Abu Hanifah states the solar year (365.25 days) should be used. However, the majority and the later relied-upon position (al-sahih) is the lunar year. The difference affects the length of the respite.

باب العنين وغيره
عورت کے لئے کوئی حق نہیں ہوگا اور اگر قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو اس کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ یہ کیسے معلوم ہوگا کہ عورت نشیبہ ہے یا با کیرہ تو صاحب عنایہ نے اس کو دریافت کرنے کی تین صورتیں بیان کی ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ عورت کی شرم گاہ میں مرغی کا چھوٹا سا انڈا داخل کیا جائے۔ اگر آسانی سے بغیر سختی کے داخل ہو جائے تو شیبہ ہے ورنہ باکرہ ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ اگر عورت کے لئے دیوار پر پیشاب کرنا ممکن ہے تو باکرہ ہے ورنہ شیبہ ہے سوم یہ کہ انڈا تو ڑ کر عورت کی شرمگاہ میں بہایا جائے پس اگر وہ اندر چلا گیا تو سمجھو کہ وہ عورت ثیبہ ہے ورنہ تو با کرہ ہے۔ واللہ اعلم۔
اگر شوہر محبوب الذکر ہے تو قاضی فوراً تفریق کر دے اگر عورت مطالبہ کرے
و ان كان مجبوبا فرق بينهما في الحال ان طلبت لانه لافائدة فى التاجيل والخصى يوجل كما يؤجل العنين لان وطيه مرجو
ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر مقطوع الذکر ہو تو دونوں میں فی الحال تفریق کر دی جائے گی بشرطیکہ عورت درخواست کرے۔ اس لئے کہ مہلت دینے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے اور خصی کو بھی مہلت دی جائے گی جیسے عنین کو دی جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس سے بھی وطی کرنے کی امید ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر مقطوع الذکر ہو تو مہلت دیئے بغیر دونوں میں تفریق کر دی جائے بشرطیکہ عورت تفریق کا مطالبہ کرے۔ کیونکہ مقطوع الذکر کی طرف سے ولی متوقع نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس کو مہلت دینے میں کوئی فائدہ نہیں ہے۔ اور آختہ ( جس کے فوطے نکال لئے گئے ہوں ) کو بھی مہلت دی جائے گی جیسے نامرد کو دی جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ وطی کرنے کی اس سے بھی امید ہے۔ یعنی آلہ تناسل موجود ہے۔ شاید کسی وقت میں اس میں وطی کی قوت پیدا ہو جائے ۔،
جب عنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی اور اس نے کہا میں نے جماع کیا عورت انکار کرتی ہے قاضی عورتوں سے معائنہ کروائے اگر وہ باکرہ کہہ دیں تو اسے اختیار دے دیا جائے اگر وہ شیبہ کہ دیں زوج قسم اٹھائے
و اذا اجل العنين سنة وقال قدجامعتها وانكرت نظر اليها النساء فان قلن هي بكر خيرت لان شهادتهن تأيدت بمؤيد و هي البكارة و ان قلن هي ثيب حلف الزوج فان نكل خيرت لتأيدها بالنكول وان حلف لا يخير ترجمه . اور جب عنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی گئی اور کہا اس نے کہ میں نے اس عورت سے جماع کر لیا ہے اور اس عورت نے انکار کیا تو اس کو عورتیں دیکھیں پس اگر عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ باکرہ موجود ہے۔ تو عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ عورتوں کی گواہی ،موید یعنی باکرہ ہونے سے قوی ہوگئی اور اگر عورتوں نے کہا کہ یہ شیبہ ہوگئی ہے تو شوہر سے قسم لی جائے گی پس اگر اس نے انکار کیا تو عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ شوہر کے انکار سے اس کی تائید ہوگئی اور اگر قسم کھا گیا تو عورت مختار نہ ہو گی۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر حاکم نے حسنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی۔ پھر اس نے کہا میں نے ایک سال کے اندر اندر جماع کر لیا اور عورت جماع کی منکر ہے تو اس کو عورت دیکھیں عورتوں کا یہ دیکھنا دو مرتبہ ہو گا ایک مرتبہ مہلت دینے سے پہلے اور ایک مرتبہ مدت گزرجانے کے بعد بہر حال اگر عورتوں نے مدت تاجیل کے بعد دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ عورت ابھی بھی باکرہ ہے تو قاضی اس عورت کو اختیار دے گا۔ پس اگر اس نے فرقت کو ترجیح دی تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اس کے باکرہ ہونے سے قوی ہوگئی ہے اس وجہ سے مرد کا یہ کہنا کہ میں جماع کر چکا ہوں غلط ہے۔ اور اگر ان عورتوں نے دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ تو شیبہ ہوگئی ہے تو شوہر سے قسم لی جائے گی پس اگر شوہر نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو بھی عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ شوہر کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دینے کی وجہ سے عورت کے دعوئی ( کہ مجھ سے جماع نہیں کیا ) کی تائید ہوگئی ہے اور اگر شو ہر قسم کھا گیا تو عورت کو اختیار نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اور شوہر کے قسم کھانے سے اس کا حق باطل ہو چکا ہے۔
اگر عورت پہلے سے شیبہ ہے مرد کا قول قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہوگا
و ان كان ثيبافي الاصل فالقول قوله مع يمينه وقد ذكرناه فان اختارت زوجها لم يكن لها بعد ذالك خيار لانها رضيت ببطلان حقها وفى التاجيل تعتبر السنة القمرية هو الصحيح ويحتسب بايام الحيض وبشهر رمضان لوجود ذالك فى السنة ولا يحتسب بمرضه ومرضها لان السنة قد تخلو عنه
ترجمہ اور اگر یہ عورت پہلے سے ثیبہ ہوتو شوہر کا قول قسم کے ساتھ قبول ہوگا اور ہم اس کو پہلے ذکر کر چکے ۔ پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر کو اختیار کر لیا تو اس کو اس کے بعد خیار نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی ہے اور مہلت کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یہی صحیح قول ہے اور ایام حیض اور رمضان کا مہینہ بھی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سال میں ان کا وجود ضروری ہے اور مرد کی بیماری اور عورت کی بیماری ( کے ایام ) شمار نہیں ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ سال کبھی بیماری سے خالی ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت پہلے سے ہی ثیبہ تھی تو اس کے شوہر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ شوہر استحقاق فرقت کا منکر ہے اور عورت مدعیہ ہے اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے جب کہ بعینہ نہ ہو پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شو ہر کو اختیار کر لیا یعنی نامرد ہونے کے باوجود اس کے ساتھ رہنا منظور کر لیا تو اس کے بعد بیوی کو تفریق کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت بذات خود اپنا حق باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نا مرد کو مہلت دینے کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۵۴ یوم اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شمسی سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۶۵ دن پورے اور ایک دن کا چوتھائی اور ایک دن کا ایک سو بیسواں حصہ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور ایک سال کی مدت میں حیض کے دن اور رمضان المبارک کا مہینہ منہا نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ سال کی مدت میں یہ ایام بھی محصوب. ناوں گے کیونکہ سال کے دوران ان ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ البتہ شوہر کی بیماری کے ایام اور عورت کی بیماری کے ایام منہا ہوں گے۔ سال کی مدت میں ان ایام کو شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بیماری کے ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بسا اوقات سال کی مدت بیماری سے خالی ہوتی ہے۔
Chapter of the Impotent and Others. The woman will have no right, and if he refuses to take an oath, he will be given a respite of one year. As for how it will be known whether the woman is a thayyib or a bikr, the author of al-‘Inayah has mentioned three ways. First, a small egg of a hen is inserted into the woman’s private part; if it goes in easily without difficulty, she is a thayyib, otherwise a bikr. Second, if it is possible for the woman to urinate against a wall, she is a bikr, otherwise a thayyib. Third, an egg is broken and its contents poured into the woman’s private part; if it goes inside, then she is a thayyib, otherwise a bikr. And Allah knows best. If the husband is a majbub (one whose penis is cut off), the judge will immediately separate them if the woman demands, because there is no benefit in giving a respite. And the khasiyy (castrated man) will be given a respite just as the ‘aneen is given a respite, because his intercourse is hoped for. Translation: And if the husband is maqtū‘ al-dhakar (penis cut off), then immediate separation will be made between the two provided the woman requests. Because there is no benefit in granting a respite. And the khasiyy will also be given a respite like the ‘aneen, because intercourse is hoped from him. Explanation: The issue is that if the husband is maqtū‘ al-dhakar, then separation is made without respite, provided the woman requests separation. Because from the side of the maqtū‘ al-dhakar, no wali (healing) is expected. Therefore, there is no benefit in granting him a respite. And the ākhta (one whose testicles have been removed) will also be given a respite like the impotent man, because intercourse is hoped from him too. That is, the penis exists, perhaps at some time the power of intercourse may develop in it. When the ‘aneen is given a respite of one year and he says, “I had intercourse with her,” and the woman denies, women are made to examine her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), then she is given the choice (khiyār), because their testimony is strengthened by the supporting evidence (mu’ayyid) which is virginity. And if they say she is a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. If he refuses, she is given the choice because of her being strengthened by his refusal. And if he takes the oath, she is given no choice. Translation: And when the ‘aneen is given a respite of one year and he says, “I had intercourse with her,” and she denies, women look at her. If they say she is a virgin (bikr), then she is given the choice. Because the testimony of the women is strengthened by the supporting evidence, which is virginity. And if they say she is a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. Then if he refuses, the woman is given the choice because of her being strengthened by his refusal. And if he takes the oath, the woman is not given the choice. Explanation: The scenario is that if the judge gave the ‘aneen a respite of one year. Then he said, “I had intercourse within the year,” and the woman denies intercourse, then women look at her. This looking by women occurs twice: once before granting respite and once after the period has passed. In any case, if after the respite period, the women see and say that the woman is still a virgin, the judge will give her the choice. Then if she chooses separation, the judge will separate them. The proof is that the women’s testimony is strengthened by her being a virgin; therefore, the man’s claim that he has had intercourse is false. And if the women see and say she has become a thayyib, then the husband is made to take an oath. Then if the husband refuses to take an oath, the woman is also given the choice, because the woman’s claim (that he has not had intercourse) is strengthened by the husband’s refusal to swear. And if the husband takes the oath, the woman will not have the choice, because the women’s testimony and the husband’s oath have nullified her right. If the woman was previously a thayyib, then the man’s statement along with his oath will be accepted. And we have mentioned this before. So if the woman chooses her husband, thereafter she has no choice, because she has consented to the nullification of her right. And regarding the respite, the lunar year is considered; this is the correct view. And the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted (within the year), because they necessarily occur in a year. And his illness and her illness are not counted, because a year may be free from illness. Translation: And if this woman had been a thayyib originally, then the husband’s statement along with his oath will be accepted, and we have mentioned this before. So if the woman chooses her husband, thereafter she has no choice, because she has consented to the nullification of her right. And in the respite, the lunar year is considered; this is the correct view. And the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted, because their occurrence in a year is necessary. And the husband’s illness and the wife’s illness are not counted, because a year may be free from illness. Explanation: The issue is that if the woman was originally a thayyib, then her husband’s statement with an oath is accepted. The reason has passed earlier that the husband is the denier (munkir) of deserving separation and the woman is the claimant (mudda‘iyah), and the statement of the denier is accepted when there is no evidence. So if the woman chose her husband, meaning she accepted to remain with him despite his impotence, then afterwards the wife will have no right to demand separation, because she has herself consented to nullify her right. The author of Hidāyah says that in the period of respite for the impotent man, the lunar year is considered, i.e., 354 days. And there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifah that the solar year is considered, i.e., 365 days, a quarter, and one hundred twentieth of a day. And in the duration of one year, the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan will not be subtracted; rather these days will also be counted in the year, because the occurrence of these days during the year is necessary. But the days of the husband’s illness and the wife’s illness will be subtracted; these days will not be counted in the year’s duration, because the occurrence of illness is not necessary; rather sometimes the year’s duration is free from illness.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with rulings related to a husband who is impotent (‘aneen) or castrated (majbub/khasiyy). It begins by stating that if a husband refuses to take an oath regarding impotency, he is given a one-year respite. The author then discusses methods to determine whether a woman is a virgin (bikr) or non-virgin (thayyib) as cited from al-‘Inayah, including inserting a hen’s egg, urinating against a wall, or pouring egg white into the private part. While these methods are mentioned, they are not part of the core legal ruling but are practical indicators.

The core ruling: If the husband is majbub (penis removed), the judge immediately separates them upon the wife’s request because there is no hope of cure. If he is khasiyy (testicles removed) or ākhta, a respite is given like the ‘aneen because intercourse is still possible. For the ‘aneen, after a one-year respite, if the husband claims he had intercourse but the wife denies, women inspect her. If they find her still a virgin, the wife is given the choice to separate or stay, as the women’s testimony is strengthened by the physical sign. If they find her a thayyib, the husband is made to take an oath. If he refuses, she gets the choice; if he swears, she loses the right to separation.

If the woman was already a thayyib before the respite, the husband’s denial of failure to have intercourse is accepted with his oath. If the wife chooses to stay with him, she cannot later demand separation.

Regarding the calculation of the one-year respite, the correct view (al-sahih) is that it is a lunar year (354 days). A narration from Abu Hanifah says solar year (365.25 days), but the relied-upon position is lunar. Days of menstruation and Ramadan are counted within the year because they necessarily occur. Days of illness for either spouse are not counted, because illness is not guaranteed to occur, so the year is calculated based on healthy days.

Key Terms
سنة قمرية (sanah qamariyyah): A lunar year of approximately 354 days, based on 12 lunar months.
سنة شمسية (sanah shamsiyyah): A solar year of approximately 365.25 days.
حیض (hayd): Menstruation; days are counted in the respite.
مرض (marad): Illness; days of illness for either spouse are not counted in the respite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following correctly describes the calculation of the one-year respite?
A) Lunar year of 354 days, excluding menstruation and Ramadan but including illness.
B) Solar year of 365 days, including all days.
C) Lunar year of 354 days, including menstruation and Ramadan but excluding illness.
D) Lunar year of 354 days, excluding all days when intercourse was not attempted.

Key Takeaway
The respite is a lunar year of 354 days, counting inevitable events but excluding illness, with the lunar year being the mufta bihi position.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Impotent Husband with a Thayyib Wife
Continues discussion of impotent husband focusing on wife's status and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a thayyib wife claims impotence and explain why the husband's statement with oath is accepted.

Core Idea
The denier's statement with oath prevails: a thayyib wife cannot prove impotence, so the husband's oath is accepted.

In cases of alleged impotence, the wife may seek annulment after a waiting period. However, if the wife is a thayyib (previously married), the husband's statement with oath is accepted because he is the denier of her claim. This lesson explains the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the wife is a thayyib (not a virgin) and claims the husband is impotent. The husband denies this.
The wife's virginity could be checked by inspection if she were a virgin, but as thayyib, that proof is unavailable.
2
Apply the legal principle
In disputes, the denier's statement with oath is accepted (qa'ida: al-munqidh yuminu). The husband is the denier of the wife's right to annulment.
The wife is the claimant (mudda'iyya), the husband is the defendant (mudda'a 'alayh).
3
Determine the consequence
If the husband swears, the wife loses her option to separate. If he refuses, the wife is given the option (khiyar).
The oath must be by Allah that he is not impotent.
4
Consider the wife's choice
If the wife chooses to stay despite the husband's impotence, she forfeits her right to seek annulment later.
She has voluntarily agreed to nullify her right.
5
Distinguish from the virgin wife
If the wife is a virgin, inspecting women may determine her status, and the husband's claim may be overridden by their testimony.
This contrast shows the importance of the wife's status.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
گزرجانے کے بعد بہر حال اگر عورتوں نے مدت تاجیل کے بعد دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ عورت ابھی بھی باکرہ ہے تو قاضی اس عورت کو اختیار دے گا۔ پس اگر اس نے فرقت کو ترجیح دی تو قاضی دونوں میں تفریق کر دے گا۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اس کے باکرہ ہونے سے قوی ہوگئی ہے اس وجہ سے مرد کا یہ کہنا کہ میں جماع کر چکا ہوں غلط ہے۔ اور اگر ان عورتوں نے دیکھ کر کہا کہ یہ تو شیبہ ہوگئی ہے تو شوہر سے قسم لی جائے گی پس اگر شوہر نے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیا تو بھی عورت کو اختیار دیا جائے گا کیونکہ شوہر کے قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دینے کی وجہ سے عورت کے دعوئی ( کہ مجھ سے جماع نہیں کیا ) کی تائید ہوگئی ہے اور اگر شوہر قسم کھا گیا تو عورت کو اختیار نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ عورتوں کی شہادت اور شوہر کے قسم کھانے سے اس کا حق باطل ہو چکا ہے۔
اگر عورت پہلے سے شیبہ ہے مرد کا قول قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہوگا
و ان كان ثيبا في الاصل فالقول قوله مع يمينه وقد ذكرناه فان اختارت زوجها لم يكن لها بعد ذالك خيار لانها رضيت ببطلان حقها وفى التاجيل تعتبر السنة القمرية هو الصحيح ويحتسب بايام الحيض وبشهر رمضان لوجود ذالك فى السنة ولا يحتسب بمرضه ومرضها لان السنة قد تخلو عنه ترجمہ اور اگر یہ عورت پہلے سے ثیبہ ہوتو شوہر کا قول قسم کے ساتھ قبول ہوگا اور ہم اس کو پہلے ذکر کر چکے ۔ پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر کو اختیار کر لیا تو اس کو اس کے بعد خیار نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے حق کو باطل کرنے پر راضی ہو گئی ہے اور مہلت کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یہی صحیح قول ہے اور ایام حیض اور رمضان کا مہینہ بھی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ سال میں ان کا وجود ضروری ہے اور مرد کی بیماری اور عورت کی بیماری ( کے ایام ) شمار نہیں ہوں گے ۔ کیونکہ سال کبھی بیماری سے خالی ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت پہلے سے ہی ثیبہ تھی تو اس کے شوہر کا قول مع الیمین معتبر ہوگا۔ دلیل سابق میں گذر چکی کہ شوہر استحقاق فرقت کا منکر ہے اور عورت مدعیہ ہے اور قول منکر کا معتبر ہوتا ہے جب کہ بعینہ نہ ہو پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر کو اختیار کر لیا یعنی نامرد ہونے کے باوجود اس کے ساتھ رہنا منظور کر لیا تو اس کے بعد بیوی کو تفریق کے مطالبہ کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت بذات خود اپنا حق باطل کرنے پر راضی ہوگئی ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نامرد کو مہلت دینے کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۵۴ یوم اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شمسی سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۶۵ دن پورے اور ایک دن کا چوتھائی اور ایک دن کا ایک سو بیسواں حصہ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور ایک سال کی مدت میں حیض کے دن اور رمضان المبارک کا مہینہ منہا نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ سال کی مدت میں یہ ایام بھی محسوب ہوں گے کیونکہ سال کے دوران ان ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ البتہ شوہر کی بیماری کے ایام اور عورت کے بیماری کے ایام منہا ہوں گے۔ سال کی مدت میں ان ایام کو شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بیماری کے ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بسا اوقات سال کی مدت بیماری سے خالی ہوتی ہے۔
1
Chapter of the impotent and others. After the passage of (the waiting period), if women (appointed to inspect) say after the specified time that this woman is still a virgin, then the judge will give her the option. If she chooses separation, the judge will separate them. The proof is that the women's testimony about her virginity has become strong, therefore the man's claim that he has had intercourse is false. And if the women say she has become a thayyib, then the husband will be asked to take an oath. If he refuses to swear, then the wife will be given the option because her claim (that he did not have intercourse) is supported by his refusal. If he swears, then she has no option because the women's testimony and the husband's oath have nullified her right. If the woman was originally a thayyib, then the husband's statement with his oath is accepted, as we have mentioned. If she chooses her husband, then after that she has no option because she has agreed to nullify her right. In the deferment (tajil), the lunar year is considered, and this is the correct view. The days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted because they exist in the year. His illness and her illness are not counted because the year may be free from illness. Explanation: The issue is that if the woman was originally a thayyib, then her husband's statement with an oath is accepted. The proof has passed before: the husband is the denier of the right to separation, and the wife is the claimant, and the statement of the denier is accepted when there is no ocular evidence. If the wife chooses her husband, meaning she consents to stay with him despite his impotence, then after that she has no right to demand separation because she has voluntarily nullified her right. The author of al-Hidayah says that in the period of deferment for the impotent, the lunar year is considered: 354 days. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the solar year is considered: 365 full days plus a quarter and one-twentieth of a day. In the period of one year, the days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are not deducted but are counted because their occurrence in the year is necessary. However, the days of the husband's illness and the wife's illness are deducted; they are not counted in the year's period because their occurrence is not necessary, and sometimes the year is free from illness.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the impotent husband (al-'anin). It addresses two main issues: first, the case where the wife is a virgin (bakr) or previously married (thayyib) after the waiting period, and second, the calculation of the waiting period (tajil). The text is a commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah, explaining the rulings and their proofs. The ruling: If after the period the inspecting women say she is still a virgin, the judge gives her the option to separate; her claim is supported by their testimony. If she is thayyib and the husband denies impotence, his statement with oath is accepted (he is the denier), but if he refuses, she gets the option. The proof is the principle that the denier's statement is accepted. If she chooses to stay, her right is forfeited. For the waiting period, the lunar year (354 days) is the relied-upon position (mu'tamad), though a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa considered the solar year. Days of menstruation and Ramadan are included because they necessarily occur within a year, but illness days are excluded because the year can be free of illness.

Key Terms
عنين ('anin): An impotent man who cannot perform sexual intercourse
ثيب (thayyib): A woman who has been previously married and no longer a virgin
تاجيل (tajil): The deferment period granted to an impotent husband to see if he can perform

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a thayyib wife claims her husband is impotent and the husband swears an oath that he is not, what is the outcome?
A) The wife is given the option to separate immediately.
B) The wife loses her option to separate.
C) The judge orders a medical examination.
D) The husband must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
The husband's statement with oath is accepted when the wife is thayyib because he is the denier, and if he swears, the wife's option to separate is lost.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Calculation of the Waiting Period (Tajil) for an Impotent Husband
Continues discussion of impotent husband focusing on the calculation of the waiting period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the length of the tajil period and identify the intra-madhhab difference regarding lunar vs. solar year.

Core Idea
The waiting period is one lunar year (354 days), counting unavoidable days like menstruation and Ramadan.

The Hanafi school grants an impotent husband a one-year grace period (tajil) before the wife may seek annulment. However, there is a difference within the school regarding whether this year is lunar or solar. This lesson clarifies the relied-upon position and explains what days are counted or excluded.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of tajil
The tajil is a deferment to see if the husband can perform intercourse. It is a condition for the wife's option to separate.
The period starts from the date the wife files a complaint.
2
State the default ruling
The correct (sahih) position is that the lunar year (354 days) is considered. This is the mufta bihi.
The lunar year follows the Islamic calendar.
3
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration that the solar year (365 days + fraction) should be used, but this is a weak narration (nawadir).
The solar year would make the wife wait longer.
4
Understand what is counted
Days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted because they inevitably occur within any year.
These are not deducted from the year.
5
Understand what is excluded
Days of illness (of husband or wife) are not counted because a year can be free of illness.
If the husband is sick for a long period, the year is not extended.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نامرد کو مہلت دینے کی مدت میں قمری سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۵۴ یوم اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ شمسی سال معتبر ہے یعنی ۳۶۵ دن پورے اور ایک دن کا چوتھائی اور ایک دن کا ایک سو بیسواں حصہ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور ایک سال کی مدت میں حیض کے دن اور رمضان المبارک کا مہینہ منہا نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ سال کی مدت میں یہ ایام بھی محسوب ہوں گے کیونکہ سال کے دوران ان ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے۔ البتہ شوہر کی بیماری کے ایام اور عورت کے بیماری کے ایام منہا ہوں گے۔ سال کی مدت میں ان ایام کو شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا کیونکہ بیماری کے ایام کا پایا جانا ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ بسا اوقات سال کی مدت بیماری سے خالی ہوتی ہے۔
1
Chapter of the impotent and others. After the passage of (the waiting period), if women (appointed to inspect) say after the specified time that this woman is still a virgin, then the judge will give her the option. If she chooses separation, the judge will separate them. The proof is that the women's testimony about her virginity has become strong, therefore the man's claim that he has had intercourse is false. And if the women say she has become a thayyib, then the husband will be asked to take an oath. If he refuses to swear, then the wife will be given the option because her claim (that he did not have intercourse) is supported by his refusal. If he swears, then she has no option because the women's testimony and the husband's oath have nullified her right. If the woman was originally a thayyib, then the husband's statement with his oath is accepted, as we have mentioned. If she chooses her husband, then after that she has no option because she has agreed to nullify her right. In the deferment (tajil), the lunar year is considered, and this is the correct view. The days of menstruation and the month of Ramadan are counted because they exist in the year. His illness and her illness are not counted because the year may be free from illness. Explanation: The issue is that if the woman was originally a thayyib, then her husband's statement with an oath is accepted. The proof has passed before: the husband is the denier of the right to separation, and the wife is the claimant, and the statement of the denier is accepted when there is no ocular evidence. If the wife chooses her husband, meaning she consents to stay with him despite his impotence, then after that she has no right to demand separation because she has voluntarily nullified her right. The author of al-Hidayah says that in the period of deferment for the impotent, the lunar year is considered: 354 days. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the solar year is considered: 365 full days plus a quarter and one-twentieth of a day. However, the days of the husband's illness and the wife's illness are deducted; they are not counted in the year's period because their occurrence is not necessary, and sometimes the year is free from illness.

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the impotent husband (al-'anin). It addresses two main issues: first, the case where the wife is a virgin (bakr) or previously married (thayyib) after the waiting period, and second, the calculation of the waiting period (tajil). Key Terms
عنين ('anin): An impotent man who cannot perform sexual intercourse
تاجيل (tajil): The deferment period granted to an impotent husband to see if he can perform
سنة قمرية (sanah qamariyyah): Lunar year, approximately 354 days, based on the Islamic calendar.

In the Hanafi school, what is the mufta bihi position regarding the length of the waiting period for an impotent husband?
A) One solar year (365 days)
B) One lunar year (354 days)
C) One Gregorian year (365 days)
D) One year minus menstrual days

Key Takeaway
The waiting period for an impotent husband is one lunar year (354 days), counting all days including cycles and Ramadan, but excluding illness days.

Can a Husband Annul Marriage for Wife's Defects? Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on annulment for wife's defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on annulment for wife's defects and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of tamakkun.

Core Idea
The husband's right is to the ability (tamakkun), not to actual enjoyment — so defects do not annul.

Marriage contracts establish mutual rights, including sexual relations. But what if the wife has a physical or mental defect? The Hanafi school holds that the husband cannot annul the marriage for any defect in the wife, while Imam al-Shafi'i allows annulment for five specific defects. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and clarifies the key concept of tamakkun.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and key principle
Identify that the husband has no option (la khiyar) to annul. The owed right is tamakkun (ability to have intercourse), not actual pleasure (istifa').
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and list the five defects
Imam al-Shafi'i allows annulment for leprosy, vitiligo, insanity, ratq (closed vagina), and qarn (vaginal obstruction). These defects prevent istifa' physically or naturally.
Natural aversion is supported by a hadith to flee from lepers.
3
Examine the Shafi'i dalil
The hadith 'Firra min al-majdhum' and natural revulsion are used to argue that the Shari'ah recognizes such aversion as grounds for annulment.
The imperative 'firra' is interpreted as a command to avoid harm.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Even total loss of intercourse through death does not annul, so partial impairment from defects is even less cause. The husband's right is tamakkun, which is present in all five cases (e.g., by surgery for ratq/qarn).
Hanafis interpret the hadith as recommended precaution, not legal nullification.

Source Text

اگر زوجہ میں کوئی عیب ہو مرد کیلئے خیار نہیں ہے، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر

و اذا كان بالزوجة عيب فلاخيار للزوج وقال الشافعى يرد بالعيوب الخمسة وهي الجذام والبرص والجنون والرتق والقرن لانها تمنع الاستيفاء حسا وطبعا والطبع مؤيد بالشرع قال عليه السلام فر من المجذوم فرارك من الاسد ولنا ان فوت الاستيفاء اصلا بالموت لا يوجب الفسخ فاختلاله بهذه العيوب اولى وهذا لان الاستيفاء من الثمرات والمستحق هو التمكن وهو حاصل
ترجمہ اور اگر بیوی میں کوئی عیب ہو، تو شوہر کو فسخ نکاح کا اختیار نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ پانچ عیوب کی وجہ سے نکاح فسخ ہو سکتا ہے جذام، برص، جنون، رتق ، قرن کیونکہ ایسے امراض حسیا یا طبعاً نفع لینے سے مانع ہیں اور طبیعت موید ہے شریعت سے چنانچہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جذامی سے ایسا بھاگ جیسے شیر سے بھاگتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ موت کی وجہ سے بالکل نفع حاصل کرنے کا فوت ہو جانا فسخ نکاح کو واجب نہیں کرتا پس ان عیوب کی وجہ سے نفع کا مختل ہو جانا بدرجہ اولی نکاح کو فسخ نہیں کرے گا اور یہ اس لئے کہ نفع حاصل کر لینا تو نکاح کا ثمرہ ہے اور مستحق صرف قابو پانے کا ہے اور یہ حاصل ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت میں کوئی عیب ہو تو ہمارے نزدیک اس عیب کی وجہ سے شوہر کو فسخ نکاح کا اختیار نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ پانچ عیوب کی وجہ سے نکاح فسخ ہو سکتا ہے وہ پانچ عیب یہ ہیں جذام یعنی کوڑھ کی بیماری برص یعنی وہ سفیدی جو بدن کے بعض حصہ پر ظاہر ہوتی ہے اور بعض پر نہیں اور کبھی کبھی پورے بدن پر ظاہر ہو جاتی ہے۔ جنون یعنی زوال عقل ہو جانا۔ رتق ، یعنی عورت کے پیشاب کے راستہ کے علاوہ کوئی دوسرا راستہ نہ ہو قرن یعنی عورت کی شرمگاہ ہڈی وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اس قدر تنگ ہو کہ اس میں مرد کے عضو تناسل کے داخل ہونے کی راہ نہ ہو۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ عیوب حسیا و طبعا مانع وطی ہیں۔ کیونکہ رتق اور قرن تو حسیا مانع وطی ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں صورتوں میں داخل کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اور جذام، برص اور جنون طبعا مانع وطی ہیں کیونکہ ان عیوب کے ہوتے ہوئے طبیعت سلیمہ جماع سے نفرت کرتی ہے۔ پھر طبیعت کی تائید میں حدیث بھی موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ آنحضرت نے فرمایا فر من المجذوم و فرارك من الاسد یعنی کوڑھ کے مریض سے اس طرح بھاگ جیسے شیر سے بھاگتا ہے۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک مجذوم نے حاضر ہو کر بیعت کا ارادہ کیا تھا تو آنحضرت نے ان کو راستہ میں کہلا بھیجا کہ تم لوٹ جاؤ ہم نے تیری بیعت کر لی اور حضرت عمر نے ایک عورت مجذومہ کو طواف کرتے دیکھ کر فرمایا کہ تو اپنے گھر میں یوں نہیں بیٹھی کہ لوگوں کو ایذا دیتی۔ چنانچہ وہ پھر بھی طواف کو نہ آئی رہے۔ اور حضرت نے جس مجذوم کے ساتھ کھانا کھایا تھا وہ اچھا ہو گیا۔ تو یہ آپ کا معجزہ تھا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ موت کی وجہ سے وطی کا فوت ہونا موجب فسخ نکاح نہیں ہے چنانچہ احد الزوجین کی موت سے مہر ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اگر ان عیوب کی وجہ سے وطی میں خلل واقع ہو جائے تو بدرجہ اولی نکاح فسخ نہیں ہو گا۔ اور ان عیوب کی وجہ سے نکاح فسخ نہ ہونا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ وطی نکاح کا ثمرہ ہے اور شوہر کا استحقاق صرف قابو پانے میں ہے اور ان تمام صورتوں میں وطی پر قابو پانا حاصل ہے چنانچہ جذام، برص اور جنون میں تو ظاہر ہے اور رتق اور قرن میں شگاف کر کے اپنا کام
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume 5. If the wife has a defect, the husband has no option (to annul the marriage). Al-Shafi'i said: He can return (annul) due to five defects: leprosy, vitiligo, insanity, ratq (closed urethra), and qarn (vaginal obstruction). Because they prevent taking benefit (istifa') physically and naturally, and nature is supported by the Shari'ah. The Prophet (SAW) said: 'Flee from the leper as you flee from a lion.' Our proof is that the total loss of taking benefit through death does not necessitate annulment, so impairment through these defects is even less likely to necessitate annulment. This is because taking benefit is a fruit (of marriage), and what is actually owed is the ability (tamakkun), and that is present. Translation: And if the wife has a defect, the husband has no option to annul the marriage. Imam Shafi'i said that the marriage can be annulled due to five defects: leprosy, vitiligo, insanity, ratq, and qarn. Because such diseases prevent taking benefit physically or naturally, and nature is supported by the Shari'ah. The Prophet (SAW) said: 'Flee from the leper as you flee from a lion.' Our proof is that the total loss of taking benefit through death does not necessitate annulment. So impairment through these defects is even less likely to necessitate annulment. This is because taking benefit is a fruit of marriage, and what is owed is only the ability, and that is present. Explanation: The issue is that if the wife has a defect, in our school the husband has no option to annul the marriage due to that defect. Imam Shafi'i says that the marriage can be annulled due to five defects. Those five defects are: leprosy (jutham) – the disease of leprosy; vitiligo (baras) – the whiteness that appears on some parts of the body; insanity (junun) – loss of intellect; ratq – the woman has no passage besides the urethra; qarn – the vagina is so tight due to bone etc. that there is no way for the male organ to enter. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that these defects prevent intercourse physically or naturally. Because ratq and qarn physically prevent intercourse, since entry is impossible in both cases. And leprosy, vitiligo, and insanity naturally prevent intercourse because a sound nature abhors intercourse with these defects. Moreover, nature is supported by hadith: the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Flee from the leper as you flee from a lion.' Another hadith: A leprous man came to pledge allegiance, so the Prophet sent word to him: 'Go back, we have accepted your allegiance.' And Umar (RA) saw a leprous woman performing tawaf and said: 'Why don't you sit in your house so that you do not harm people?' So she never came for tawaf again. And the Prophet ate with a leprous man who was cured; that was his miracle. Our proof is that the loss of intercourse due to death does not necessitate annulment; indeed, the mahr does not drop due to death of either spouse. So if intercourse is impaired by these defects, it follows that the marriage is not annulled. The reason the marriage is not annulled is that intercourse is a fruit of marriage, and the husband's right is only to the ability (tamakkun), and in all these cases the ability to have intercourse is present. In leprosy, vitiligo, and insanity it is possible, and in ratq and qarn one can make an incision and accomplish the act.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether the husband has the right to annul the marriage (faskh al-nikah) due to defects in the wife. The Hanafi position: The husband has no option (khiyar) to annul the marriage for any defect in the wife, because the marriage contract is not invalidated by defects; the right to sexual enjoyment is a fruit of marriage, but what is actually owed is the ability (tamakkun) to have intercourse, which is present even with these defects. The Shafi'i position: The marriage can be annulled due to five specific defects: leprosy, vitiligo, insanity, ratq (closed vagina), and qarn (vaginal obstruction). Their proof: These defects prevent intercourse either physically (ratq and qarn) or naturally (the other three, as nature abhors them), and the Shari'ah supports natural aversion, as shown by the hadith to flee from a leper. The Hanafi response: Even total loss of intercourse through death does not annul the marriage (e.g., if one spouse dies, the marriage is terminated by death, not annulled; the mahr is not dropped). Therefore, partial impairment through defects should not annul it either. The key principle is that the husband is only entitled to the ability to have intercourse, not actual enjoyment. In all these cases, intercourse is possible (e.g., by making an incision in ratq/qarn).

Key Terms
جذام (jutham): Leprosy, a disfiguring disease
برص (baras): Vitiligo, patches of white skin
رتق (ratq): A vaginal defect where the only opening is the urethra
قرن (qarn): Vaginal obstruction due to bone or flesh
تمكن (tamakkun): The ability to have sexual intercourse, regardless of actual enjoyment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why doesn't a husband have the right to annul the marriage due to the wife's leprosy?
A) Because leprosy is not considered a defect in Shari'ah.
B) Because the husband's right is only to tamakkun, not actual enjoyment.
C) Because the Prophet (SAW) forbade annulment for any reason.
D) Because the wife must consent to annulment.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a husband cannot annul for wife's defects because the marriage contract only guarantees the ability (tamakkun) to have intercourse, not actual enjoyment.

Nikah — Marriage

Wife's Option for Husband's Non-Sexual Defects
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wife's option for husband's defects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on wife's option for husband's insanity or leprosy and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Sheikhayn and Imam Muhammad, including the qiyas argument and its rebuttal.

Core Idea
A wife cannot annul for insanity or leprosy because these do not destroy the purpose of marriage — only complete impotence does.

In this passage, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a wife can annul her marriage if her husband suffers from insanity (junun), vitiligo (baras), or leprosy (juzam). The two senior imams, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sheikhayn), hold that she has no option, while Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani argues she does. The disagreement turns on whether these diseases are analogous to jabb (penile amputation) and 'inna (impotence), where the wife is granted the right to annul. We will unpack the reasoning on both sides and see why the Sheikhayn's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, clearly state the ruling of the Sheikhayn and the ruling of Imam Muhammad. Note that the Sheikhayn's view is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
2
Understand Muhammad's qiyas argument
Muhammad compares these diseases to jabb and 'inna, arguing that both cause harm (darar) to the wife, so she should have the option to annul to remove that harm.
3
Analyse the Sheikhayn's rebuttal and distinction
The Sheikhayn argue that the default is no option, and jabb/'inna are exceptions because they completely destroy the purpose of marriage (intercourse), while these diseases do not. Therefore, the analogy fails.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the Sheikhayn, the wife remains married and cannot annul; according to Muhammad, she may choose to annul.
