Ruling on Indirect Marriage Proposals (Ta'rīḍ) to Women in Iddah
Ruling with Qur'anic proof on indirect proposals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit (tasrīḥ) and indirect (ta'rīḍ) marriage proposals during iddah and state the Hanafi ruling for each with its Qur'anic basis.

Core Idea
The Qur'an allows indirect proposals during iddah but forbids explicit ones.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on proposing marriage to a woman during her iddah. The key distinction is between explicit statements (tasrīḥ) and indirect hints (ta'rīḍ). The Qur'an itself provides the basis for this distinction, allowing hints while prohibiting explicit commitment. We will explore the evidence and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Two Categories
The act is proposing marriage to a woman in her iddah. This is divided into explicit proposal (tasrīḥ) and indirect proposal (ta'rīḍ). The ruling depends on which category is used.
Explicit means clear words of marriage; indirect means suggestive words that imply the desire.
2
Locate the Dalil for Each Ruling
The prohibition of explicit proposals is based on the verse 'Do not resolve on the marriage contract until the book reaches its term' (Qur'an 2:235). The permissibility of indirect proposals is from the same verse: 'There is no sin upon you concerning that which you offer of hint.'
Both rulings come from the same verse, highlighting the importance of linguistic nuance.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (Legal Link)
The word 'ta'rīḍ' appears in the verse and is interpreted by the Prophet (peace be upon him) and companions as any indirect expression. The prohibition is on 'azm (resolution) on the marriage contract, which implies explicit commitment.
The Hanafi understanding relies on the literal meaning of 'ta'rīḍ'.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Disagreement)
While all schools agree on the basic distinction, there may be differences in what counts as ta'rīḍ. The Hanafi school is relatively broad, considering statements like 'I wish to marry' or 'You are beautiful' as ta'rīḍ.
The ikhtilaf is about the scope, not the principle.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih (Preference)
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi (operative ruling). It is based on clear Qur'anic text and Prophetic practice. There is no need for preferring one view over another since the evidence is strong.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is widely relied upon.

Source Text

Ashraf al-Hidayah: Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, Volume 5. It is not appropriate to give a marriage proposal to a woman in iddah, but there is no harm in making an indirect proposal (ta'rīḍ). Because Allah Almighty says: "And there is no sin upon you concerning that which you offer of hint [of marriage] to women..." (Qur'an 2:235). You may say something indirectly or keep the intention of marriage hidden in your hearts. Allah knows that you will mention them [in your hearts], but do not make a contract of marriage with them until the appointed term reaches its end, except that you say a word according to the norm. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "The word 'sar' (secret) means marriage." Ibn Abbas said: "Ta'rīḍ is that one says, 'I desire to marry.'" And regarding the proper word (qawl ma'rūf), it is narrated from Sa'id ibn Jubayr that he said: "You say, 'I am inclined to you,' or 'I wish that we could be together.'"
Commentary: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri says: It is not appropriate to give a marriage proposal to women in iddah, because Allah's command is: "Do not resolve on the marriage contract until the book reaches its term" (Qur'an 2:235), meaning do not intend the marriage contract with women in iddah until their waiting period ends. But there is no harm in making an indirect proposal. The proof is the verse: "And there is no sin upon you concerning that which you offer of hint [of marriage] to women..." The translation was given earlier. Ta'rīḍ is to mention something that implies something else. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Sar means marriage." So the meaning is: do not make a promise of marriage to women in iddah. Ibn Abbas said: Ta'rīḍ is to say, 'I want to marry,' or 'I wish I could get a righteous woman.' Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: The proper word is to say, 'I am inclined to you,' or 'I wish for us to live together,' or something similar, e.g., telling the woman in iddah, 'You are very beautiful, very righteous.' The conclusion is that everything may be said by hints, but one must not explicitly mention marriage.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Hanafi school, presented by the commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) explaining the matn of al-Hidayah. The issue is the permissibility of proposing marriage to a woman during her iddah (waiting period after divorce or widowhood). The ruling distinguishes between two types of proposals: explicit (tasrīḥ) and indirect (ta'rīḍ). Explicit proposals are forbidden based on Qur'an 2:235 ("do not resolve on the marriage contract..."), while indirect proposals are permitted based on the same verse ("there is no sin upon you concerning that which you offer of hint..."). The commentator defines ta'rīḍ as any statement that implies the desire for marriage without directly saying it, such as 'I wish to marry' or 'I am inclined to you.' He quotes the Prophet's statement that the word 'sar' (secret) means marriage, implying that keeping the intention hidden is acceptable. The Hanafi position is clear: ta'rīḍ is allowed, but explicit proposals are forbidden until the iddah ends. The authority weight is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is a standard ruling in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
تعريض (ta'rīḍ): An indirect or suggestive statement that implies a desire for marriage without explicitly stating it.
خطبة (khitbah): Marriage proposal, either explicit or indirect.

Key Takeaway

Nikah — Marriage

Establishing Lineage via Firash (Marital Bed)
Ruling with proof on establishing paternity via firash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on establishing lineage for a child born six months after marriage in a conditional divorce scenario, identify the proof (al-walad li al-firash), and explain the role of the minimum pregnancy duration.

Core Idea
The child belongs to the marital bed; lineage is established if birth occurs exactly six months after marriage.

This lesson explores a classic Hanafi scenario where a man conditions a divorce upon marriage, and the wife gives birth exactly six months later. The ruling establishes that the child is the husband's legitimate offspring and full mahr is due. We will examine the legal reasoning, the proof from hadith, and the crucial role of the minimum pregnancy period as a condition for establishing lineage.

Guided Path
1
Parse the scenario
Identify the key elements: a man says 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' He then marries her, and she gives birth exactly six months from the marriage date.
The divorce takes effect immediately at the moment of marriage.
2
Determine the timing of conception
The minimum duration of pregnancy is six lunar months. Since the child is born six months after marriage, conception occurred at the same time as the marriage and the divorce.
This timing is critical: it means conception happened during the brief window when the marriage was valid.
3
Apply the firash principle
The hadith 'al-walad li al-firash' (the child belongs to the marital bed) attributes the child to the husband. Imam al-Karkhi interprets firash as the marriage contract itself, not physical cohabitation.
Thus, the mere existence of a valid marriage contract at the time of conception is sufficient for lineage.
4
Derive the consequences
Since lineage is established, the child is legally the son of the husband. Additionally, full mahr (dower) is due because the husband is deemed to have had intercourse (wati' hukman).
If the child were born before six months (conception before marriage) or after more than six months (possible conception after divorce), lineage would not be established.
5
Evaluate the proof
The primary proof is the mutawatir hadith. The wajh al-dalalah is the imperative attribution 'li al-firash' – ownership/attribution to the husband. The text also notes that lineage is established with caution (ihtiyat).
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is agreed upon within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ثبوت النسب
ترجمہ (یہ) باب ثبوت نسب ( کے احکام کے بیان میں ) ہے۔
باب ثبوت النست
تشریح مصنف نے سابق میں معدہ کی انواع ذوات الحیض ، ذوات الا شہر اور ذوات الاحتمال ) کو بیان فرمایا ہے۔ اس باب میں ذوات الاحمال کے لازم یعنی ثبوت نسب کا ذکر فرمائیں گے۔
مرد نے کہا ان تزوجت فلانه فهي طالق اس کے ساتھ نکاح کیا اس نے
نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ میں بچہ جنا یہ اس کا بیٹا ہے اور مرد پر مہر لازم ہے
ومن قال ان تزوجت فلانة فهى طالق فتزوجها فولدت ولد الستة اشهر من يوم تزوجها فهو ابنه وعليه المهراما النسب فلانها فراشه لانها لما جاءت بالولد لستة اشهر من وقت النكاج فقد جاءت به لاقل منها من وقت الطلاق فكان العلوق قبله فى حالة النكاح والتصور ثابت بان تزوجها وهو يخالطها فوافق الانزال النكاح والنسب يحتاط فى اثباته واما المهر فلانه لماثبت النسب منه جعل واطيا حكما فتاكد المهربه
ترجمہ اور جس مرد نے کہا کہ اگر میں فلاں عورت سے نکاح کروں تو وہ طالقہ ہے۔ پھر اس سے نکاح کیا۔ نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ پر اس نے بچہ جنا ، تو یہ بچہ اس مرد کا بیٹا ہے اور اس پر پورا مہر واجب ہے۔ بہر حال نسب تو اسلئے کہ وہ عورت اس مرد کی فراش ہے ۔ کیونکہ جب نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ پر اس نے بچہ جنا تو طلاق کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ لائی۔ پس علوق طلاق سے پہلے نکاح کی حالت میں ہوا اور امکان بھی ثابت ہے۔ اس طرح پر کہ مرد نے اس عورت سے وطی کرنے کی حالت میں نکاح کیا اور نکاح ہو جانے پر انزال ہو کر نطفہ ٹھہر گیا اور نسب ثابت کرنے میں احتیاط کی جاتی ہے اور بہر حال مہر تو اسلئے کہ جب اس سے نسب ثابت ہو گیا تو حکما ولی کرنے والا قرار پایا۔ پس اس کی وجہ سے پورا مہر ثابت ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ کسی شخص نے کہا کہ اگر میں فلاں عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کروں تو اس کو طلاق ہے۔ پھر اس شخص نے اس عورت کے ساتھ نکاح کیا اور اس عورت نے نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ پر ایک بچہ جنا ۔ تو یہ بچہ اس کا فرزند ہوگا۔ یعنی بچہ کا نسب اس سے ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اس شخص پر پورا مہر واجب ہوگا اور اگر چھ ماہ سے زائکہ مدت میں بچہ پیدا ہوا یا چھ ماہ سے کم میں پیدا ہوا تو اس شخص سے نسب ثبات نہیں ہوگا۔ پہلی صورت میں تو اسلئے نہیں ثابت ہوگا کہ جب بچہ نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے زائد میں پیدا ہوا تو ممکن ہے کہ علوق طلاق کے بعد ہوا۔ لہذا نہ نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا اور نہ عورت پر عدت واجب ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں نسب اسلئے ثابت نہیں ہوگا کہ جب بچہ نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں پیدا ہوا تو یقیناً علوق نکاح سے پہلے ہے۔ لہذا اس صورت میں بھی نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ بہر حال متن کے مسئلہ میں ثبوت نسب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ عورت اس کی فراش ہے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا الولد للفراش و للعاهر الحجر یعنی بچہ صاحب فراش کا ہوتا ہے اور زانی کیلئے پتھر ہوتا ہے اور امام کرختی نے فراش کی تفسیر عقد کے ساتھ کی ہے۔ یعنی بچہ صاحب عقد نکاح کیلئے ہوتا ہے۔
Chapter of Establishing Lineage. Translation: This is the chapter on the rulings of establishing lineage. Chapter of Establishing Lineage. Explanation: Previously the author mentioned the types of 'iddah (for women with menstruation, months, and pregnancy). In this chapter, he will mention the requirement of pregnancy, i.e., establishing lineage. A man said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' He married her, and she gave birth to a child six months from the day of marriage. This child is his son, and a full mahr (dower) is obligatory upon him. And whoever said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced,' then he married her, and she gave birth to a child after six months from the day he married her, then it is his son, and the mahr is upon him. As for lineage, it is because she is his firash (marital bed). Because when she brought the child at six months from the time of marriage, she brought it at less than six months from the time of divorce. Thus, the conception occurred before the divorce, in the state of marriage, and the possibility is established: because he married her while he was intimate with her, and ejaculation coincided with the marriage, and the sperm settled. And lineage is treated with caution in its establishment. As for the mahr, because when lineage is established from him, he is considered a husband (wati') legally, so the mahr is confirmed. Translation: And whoever said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' Then he married her. She gave birth to a child at six months from the time of marriage. Then this child is his son, and the full mahr is obligatory upon him. As for lineage, it is because that woman is his firash. Because when she brought the child at six months from the time of marriage, she brought it at less than six months from the time of divorce. Thus, conception occurred before the divorce, in the state of marriage, and the possibility is established. In such a way that the man married her while he was intimate with her, and upon marriage, ejaculation occurred, and the sperm settled. And lineage is treated with caution in its establishment. As for the mahr, because when lineage was established from him, he became legally considered a husband (wati'). So due to it, the full mahr is established. Explanation: The issue is that a person said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' Then that person married that woman, and that woman gave birth to a child six months from the time of marriage. Then this child will be his offspring. That is, the child's lineage will be established from him, and full mahr will be obligatory upon that person. If the child is born after more than six months or less than six months, then lineage will not be established from that person. In the first case, it will not be established because when the child is born after more than six months from marriage, it is possible that conception occurred after divorce. Hence, lineage will not be established, nor will 'iddah be obligatory upon the woman. In the second case, lineage will not be established because when the child is born in less than six months from marriage, certainly conception occurred before marriage. Hence, in this case as well, lineage will not be established. Nevertheless, in the issue of the matn, the proof of establishing lineage is that this woman is his firash, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The child belongs to the firash, and the fornicator gets nothing.' That is, the child belongs to the owner of the firash, and for the fornicator is stones. And Imam al-Karkhi interpreted firash as the marriage contract. That is, the child belongs to the owner of the marriage contract.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the establishment of lineage (nasab) when a man conditions a divorce upon marriage. The scenario: a man says, 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' He then marries her, and she gives birth exactly six months from the marriage date. The ruling: the child is his son (lineage established) and he must pay the full mahr (dower). The reasoning is based on the concept of firash (marital bed). The child came at six months from marriage, which is less than six months from the conditional divorce (since divorce occurs at the moment of marriage? Actually, the divorce was conditional: if he marries her, she is divorced. So upon marriage, the divorce takes effect immediately. Thus, the divorce occurs at the same moment as marriage. But the child is born six months after marriage, meaning six months after divorce. However, normal minimum pregnancy is six months. So if she gives birth at six months from marriage, it means the conception occurred at the time of marriage (since pregnancy from time of conception to birth is at least six months). So the conception was at the time of marriage, which is before the divorce (since divorce happens at the exact moment of marriage). Therefore, the child was conceived during lawful marital intercourse (since marriage was valid at that moment). Hence, the child is attributed to the husband. The text also explains that if the child is born after more than six months, it's possible conception was after divorce, so no lineage. If less than six months, conception was before marriage, so no lineage. The proof is the hadith 'al-walad li al-firash' (the child belongs to the marital bed). Imam al-Karkhi interprets 'firash' as the marriage contract, meaning that the child is attributed to the husband as long as the child is born within a valid marriage with possibility of conception. The mahr is due because the husband is deemed to have had intercourse (due to the lineage), so full mahr is confirmed.

Key Terms
ثبوت نسب (thubut nasab): The legal establishment of paternity/lineage between a child and the alleged father.
فراش (firash): The marital bed, metaphorically referring to the lawful marriage relationship; the child belongs to the husband of the marriage.
علوق (uluq): Conception, the beginning of pregnancy.
مہر (mahr): Dower, the payment given by the husband to the wife upon marriage, due in full upon consummation or valid marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the given scenario, why is the child attributed to the husband even though a conditional divorce was pronounced upon marriage?
A) Because the child was born after exactly six months, which is the minimum pregnancy duration, so conception occurred at the time of marriage/divorce, which is within a valid marriage.
B) Because the conditional divorce is invalid, so the marriage remains intact.
C) Because the woman's testimony is accepted over the husband's.
D) Because the husband admitted paternity.

Key Takeaway
A child born exactly six months after marriage is attributed to the husband, and full mahr is due, based on the hadith 'al-walad li al-firash' and the minimum pregnancy period.

Conditional Divorce and Paternity within Six Months of Marriage
Ruling on paternity and mahr in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity and mahr when a child is born exactly six months after a conditional divorce, and explain how istihsān establishes lineage despite remote possibility of intercourse.

Core Idea
A child born six months after marriage is presumed the husband's even if conception seems far-fetched, because lineage is cautiously established.

Imagine a man says, 'If I marry Fatima, she is divorced,' then marries her. Exactly six months later, she gives birth. Is the child his? Does he owe mahr? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling that declares the child his son and the mahr wajib, based on the hadith 'al-waladu lil-firāsh' and the principle of istihsān. We will walk through the legal reasoning, the proof, and the responses to objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
The case: a conditional divorce threat before marriage. The child is born exactly six months after the marriage contract. The ruling: the child is the husband's son, and full mahr is wajib.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith: 'al-waladu lil-firāsh wa lil-ʿāhir al-ḥajar' is cited. The term 'firāsh' is interpreted by Imam al-Karkhī as the marriage contract itself.
This interpretation is key; other schools require actual intercourse possibility.
3
Understand the istihsān reasoning
Since the child arrives at the minimum pregnancy period from marriage, conception must have occurred during marriage. Even if the scenario of intercourse at the contract moment is rare, lineage is cautiously established by istihsān.
Istihsān departs from strict analogy (qiyās) in favor of caution (ihtiyāṭ).
4
Analyze the counterargument and response
Objection: the possibility of intercourse at contract is far-fetched. Response: possibility is acceptable through the karamah of awliyā' or by the principle that marriage itself implies cohabitation. The text rebuts the view that mere marriage suffices without any possibility.
This shows the nuanced Hanafi position: possibility is required but interpreted broadly.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in cases where spouses are geographically distant, the Hanafi position still establishes paternity, while stricter views would not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال ان تزوجت فلانة فهي طالق فتزوجها فولدت ولد الستة اشهر من يوم تزوجها فهو ابنه وعليه المهر. اما النسب فلانها فراشه لانها لما جاءت بالولد لستة اشهر من وقت النكاح فقد جاءت به لاقل منها من وقت الطلاق فكان العلوق قبله فى حالة النكاح والتصور ثابت بان تزوجها وهو يخالطها فوافق الانزال النكاح والنسب يحتاط فى اثباته. واما المهر فلانه لماثبت النسب منه جعل واطيا حكما فتاكد المهر به. اذا جاءت به لاقل من ستة اشهر من وقت النكاح لا يثبت النسب لان العلوق قبل النكاح يقينا. واذا جاءت به لاكثر من ستة اشهر يحتمل العلوق بعد الطلاق فلا يثبت. والدليل على اثبات النسب في هذه المسئلة قوله عليه السلام: الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر. وفسر امام الكرخي الفراش بالعقد. ثم بين صاحب الهداية انه اذا جاءت به لستة اشهر من وقت النكاح لزم ان يكون قد جاءت به لاقل من ستة اشهر من وقت الطلاق، فيكون العلوق في حالة النكاح قبل الطلاق، وثبوت التصور ممكن بان تزوجها وهو يخالطها، فانزل عند العقد فاستقر النطفة. فان قيل هذا التصور بعيد وامر نادر، قلنا النسب يحتاط في اثباته فثبت استحسانا. وقال بعض المشايخ لا حاجة الى هذا التكلف، بل يكفي وجود الفراش واعتبار امكان الدخول، لان النكاح يقوم مقام الوطي. وعورض بقولهم: ثبت النسب بشرط تصور الوطي، كما في الصغير وغيره. واجيب عن قول بعض المشايخ: ان التصور موجود في حق الزوج بتقدير كرامة الاولياء. واما المهر فلما ثبت النسب صار واطيا حكما فوجب المهر كاملا.
And whoever said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced,' then he married her, and she gave birth to a child at six months from the day he married her, then it is his son and the mahr is incumbent on him. As for lineage, because she is his bed (farāsh), since when she brought the child at six months from the time of marriage, she brought it at less than six months from the time of divorce. Thus conception was before the divorce in the state of marriage, and the mental image is established that he married her and he was having intercourse with her, and (the) emission (coincided) with marriage. And lineage is cautiously established. As for mahr, because when lineage is established from him, he is made legally a cohabiter so the mahr is confirmed. If she brings the child at less than six months from the time of marriage, lineage is not established because conception is definitely before marriage. If she brings it at more than six months, conception may be after divorce so it is not established. The proof for establishing lineage in this issue is his statement (peace be upon him): 'The child belongs to the bed.' Al-Karkhī interpreted the bed as the contract. Then the author of Al-Hidāyah explained that if she brings it at six months from the time of marriage, it is necessary that she brought it at less than six months from the time of divorce, so conception occurred during marriage before divorce, and the scenario is possible if he married her while having intercourse with her and ejaculated at the contract and the sperm settled. If it is said: 'This scenario is far-fetched and rare,' we say: lineage is cautiously established, so it is established by istihsān. Some mashā'ikh said there is no need for this complexity; rather the existence of the bed and the possibility of entry suffice because marriage stands in place of intercourse. This was countered by saying: lineage is established on condition of possibility of intercourse, as in the minor etc. And it was answered regarding the statement of some mashā'ikh: possibility exists for the husband by assuming the karamah of awliyā'. As for mahr, when lineage was established, he became legally a cohabiter so full mahr became obligatory.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof from the chapter on establishing lineage (thubūt al-nasab). The case is a conditional divorce: a man says, 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced,' then he marries her. If she gives birth at exactly six months from the marriage, the child's paternity is established as his son and he must pay the full mahr. The reasoning is that since six months from marriage is the minimum period of pregnancy, the child must have been conceived before the divorce (while still in marriage). Although conception during the marriage contract itself may seem unlikely, the Law esteems caution in establishing lineage, so the ruling is based on istihsān (juristic preference). The author then addresses objections: some earlier scholars argued that mere existence of marriage (farāsh) suffices without requiring actual physical possibility, but this is countered by the example of a minor husband where possibility is necessary. The response defends possibility by invoking the karamah of saints—Allah may shorten distances. Finally, the mahr is full because legal cohabitation is deemed to have occurred.

Key Terms
فراش (farāsh): The marriage bed; figuratively, the marital bond that establishes paternity. In this context, it is interpreted as the marriage contract (al-'aqd) by Imam al-Karkhī.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that departs from strict analogy (qiyās) in favor of a more suitable ruling based on underlying principles or public interest.
علوق (ʿulūq): Conception; the moment when the sperm meets the ovum and pregnancy begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the conditional divorce scenario, why is the child's paternity established if born exactly six months from marriage?
A) Because the mother admits the husband is the father.
B) Because six months is the maximum period of pregnancy.
C) Because the child came at less than six months from the divorce, indicating conception during marriage.
D) Because the man explicitly acknowledged the child.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a child born six months after a conditional divorce marriage is the husband's son, and full mahr is wajib, based on cautious paternity establishment and istihsān even if the possibility of intercourse is remote.

Paternity of Child Born to Revocably Divorced Woman
Ruling on paternity from a revocably divorced woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a child is attributed to a revocably divorced woman's ex-husband and distinguish whether the birth constitutes a raj'a.

Core Idea
Lineage is established if birth occurs within two years; after two years, it is a silent raj'a.

When a revocably divorced woman gives birth, the timing of the birth relative to the divorce determines both the child's paternity and whether the husband has taken her back. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi position, which relies on the maximum pregnancy period of two years and the principle 'al-waladu lil-firāsh'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the key time frames
Note the two thresholds: birth before two years, at two years, and after two years. Each triggers a different ruling.
2
Determine lineage (nasad)
When birth occurs within or at two years, and the woman does not admit the expiry of her iddah, the child is attributed to the ex-husband.
3
Determine the effect on the woman's marital status
If birth occurs before two years, she becomes bā'ina (irrevocably divorced) because the iddah ends with birth. If after two years, the birth itself constitutes a raj'a (return to marriage).
4
Understand the reasoning behind the two-year maximum
The Hanafi school holds that the maximum period of pregnancy can be two years. This is the basis for the rulings. The proof is the hadith 'al-waladu lil-firāsh' and qiyas.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Shafi'is set a maximum of four years, so the time window for establishing lineage after divorce is longer. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويثبت نسب ولد المطلقة الرجعية اذا جاءت به لسنتين او اكثر مالم تقر بانقضاء عدتها لاحتمال العلوق فى حالة لجوازانها تكون ممتدة الطهر وان جاءت به لاقل من سنتين بانت من زوجها بانقضاء العدة وثبت نسبه لوجود العلوق فى النكاح اوفى العدة ولا يصير مراجعا لانه يحتمل العلوق قبل الطلاق ويحتمل بعده فلا يصير مراجعا بالشك. وان جاءت به لاكثر من سنتين كانت رجعة لان العلوق بعد الطلاق والظاهر انه منه لانتقاء الزنا منها فيصير بالوطي مراجعا.
He said: And the lineage of the child of a revocably divorced woman is established if she brings it at two years or more, as long as she does not admit to the expiry of her 'iddah, due to the possibility of conception during the 'iddah period because she may be one whose menses are protracted. If she brings it at less than two years, she becomes bā'ina from her husband due to the expiry of 'iddah, and his lineage is established because conception occurred in marriage or in the 'iddah. And he does not become a raj'a (by that) because conception may be before divorce and may be after, so he does not become a raj'a by doubt. And if she brings it at more than two years, it is a raj'a, because conception occurred after divorce and the apparent is that it is from him due to the absence of adultery from her, so he becomes a raj'a by intercourse.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on lineage for a child born to a revocably divorced woman (muttallaqa raj'iyya). The general rule: if she gives birth within two years (or up to two years) from the divorce, the child's lineage is established with the ex-husband, unless she herself admits that her 'iddah has already expired. The reason is that the 'iddah of a revocably divorced woman can last up to two years (according to the Hanafi view that the maximum period of pregnancy is two years). If she gives birth before two years, she becomes bā'ina (irrevocably divorced) because the 'iddah expires at birth, but lineage is still established because conception must have occurred during the marriage or 'iddah. However, this birth alone does not constitute a raj'a (return to marriage) because it is uncertain whether conception happened before or after divorce. If she gives birth after two years (more than two years from divorce), it is considered a raj'a—meaning the husband becomes a revocable returnee—because conception must have occurred after divorce and since she is not an adulteress, the child is attributed to him, and by that intercourse (presumed), he has effectively taken her back. The ruling hinges on the Hanafi maximum pregnancy period of two years, and the principle that the child is attributed to the marriage bed unless the woman admits expiry of 'iddah.

Key Terms
مطلقة رجعية (muṭallaqa rajʿiyya): A woman who has been given a revocable divorce (ṭalāq rajʿī), meaning the husband can take her back without a new marriage contract during her ʿiddah period.
عدة (ʿidda): The waiting period a divorced woman must observe before remarrying. For a non-pregnant woman, three menstrual cycles; for a pregnant woman, until delivery; for a revocably divorced woman, it is the same but the husband can return.
رجعة (rajʿa): The act of the husband taking back his revocably divorced wife during her ʿiddah, which restores the marital relationship without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is the child of a revocably divorced woman attributed to her ex-husband?
A) If she gives birth at any time after divorce.
B) If she gives birth within two years and does not admit that her ʿiddah has ended.
C) Only if she gives birth within six months of divorce.
D) If the husband acknowledges paternity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school attributes the child to the ex-husband if born within two years of a revocable divorce, and after two years the birth itself is a return to marriage.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Lineage and Revocation after Revocable Divorce
Main ruling with three time-based scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lineage and revocation for a revocably divorced woman for each of the three childbirth time periods relative to the divorce.

Core Idea
For a revocably divorced woman, lineage is established if the child is born within two years, but revocation only if birth occurs after two years.

This lesson examines the detailed ruling from al-Hidayah on the lineage of a child born to a woman who received a revocable divorce. The Hanafi school provides a precise framework based on the time between divorce and birth, determining both paternity and whether the husband's revocation (raj'a) occurs. Understanding these time-based rules is crucial for correctly applying the law in family matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the status of the woman
The woman is a revocably divorced woman (muttalaqa raj'iyya) in her iddah. Intercourse with her is lawful during this period.
She is still considered married for certain purposes.
2
Determine the time of childbirth relative to the divorce
There are three scenarios: birth in less than 2 years, birth at exactly 2 years or more but not exceeding 2 years (i.e., within 2 years), and birth after more than 2 years.
The text uses 'لسنتين او اکثر' (two years or more) and 'لاكثر من سنتين' (more than two years) as separate categories.
3
Apply the ruling for each scenario
For less than 2 years: woman becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) because iddah ends by delivery, but lineage is established (conception could be during marriage or iddah). Husband does NOT become revoker. For 2 years or more (within 2 years): lineage is established, and husband may or may not become revoker depending on whether conception is clearly after divorce; the text says if more than 2 years, revocation occurs. For more than 2 years: revocation is certain because conception is definitely after divorce.
The key distinction: within 2 years, revocation is doubtful; beyond 2 years, it is certain.
4
Understand the role of the woman's admission
If the woman admits that her iddah has ended (even if she gives birth within 2 years), lineage is not established because then there is no possibility of conception during marriage or iddah.
This overrides the presumption of the marital bed.
5
Synthesize the legal effects
For each scenario, state: lineage status (established or not), revocation status (occurs or not), and whether the woman becomes bain or remains in iddah.
Use the table in the commentary to summarize.

قال ويثبت نسب ولد المطلقة الرجعية اذا جاءت به لسنتين او اکثر مالم تقر بانقضاء عدتها لاحتمال العلوق فى حالة الجواز انها تكون ممتدة الطهر وان جاءت به لاقل من سنتين بالت من زوجها بانقضاء العدة وثبت نسبه لوجود العلوق فى النكاح اوفى العدة ولا يصير مراجعا لانه يحتمل العلوق قبل الطلاق ويحتمل بعده فلا يصير مراجعا بالشك وان جاءت به لاكثر من سنتين كانت رجعة لان العلوق بعد الطلاق والظاهر انه منه لانتقاء الزنا منها فيصير بالوطى مراجعا
ترجمہ فرمایا کہ جس عورت کو طلاق رجعی دی گئی ہے۔ اسکے بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ اس نے بچہ دو سال یا دو سال سے زیادہ میں جنا ہو جب تک کہ عورت نے اپنی عدت گذر جانے کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ احتمال ہے کہ عدت کی حالت میں نطفہ رہا ہو۔ اسلئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ یہ عورت ممتدۃ الطہر ہو اور اگر اس عورت نے دو سال سے کم میں بچہ جنا ہو تو وہ اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو گئی۔ عدت گذر جانے کی وجہ سے
اور بنچہ کا نسب (شوہر سے) ثابت ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ علوق (نطفہ ) نکاح میں پایا گیا یا عدت میں اور شوہر رجعت کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ علوق قبل الطلاق کا احتمال ہے اور بعد الطلاق کا بھی احتمال ہے۔ لہذا شوہر شک کی وجہ سے رجعت کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا اور اگر اس عورت نے دو سال سے زائد میں بچہ جنا تو رجعت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ علوق بعد الطلاق ہے اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ نطفہ اسی مرد سے ہو ۔ اسلئے کہ عورت سے زنا منتفی ہے۔ پس وہ ولی سے مراجعت کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت جس کو اس کے شوہر نے طلاق رجعی دی ہے۔ اسنے طلاق کے وقت سے دو سال پر یا دو سال سے زیادہ پر بچہ جنا تو شوہر سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ عورت نے عدت گذر جانے کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ یہ عورت ممتدۃ الطہر ہو اور طہر کے دراز ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی عدت دراز ہوگئی ہو اور شوہر نے عدت کے زمانہ میں ولی کر لی ہو۔ کیونکہ معتدہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ ولی کرنا حلال ہے۔ پس اس وطی سے رجعت بھی ثابت ہوگی اور بچہ کا نسب بھی ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
اور اگر دو سال سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا ہے تو یہ عورت اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو گئی اور اس بچہ کا نسب اس کے شوہر سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ بائنہ تو اسلئے ہو گئی کہ وضع حمل کی وجہ سے بائنہ ہو جاتی ہے۔
اور ثبوت نسب کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ولی حالت نکاح میں کی گئی ہے تب تو ظاہر ہے اور اگر عدت میں وطی کی گئی ہے تب بھی نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ معدہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کرنا شرعا حلال ہے۔ لیکن شوہر اس وطی سے مراجعت کرنے والا شمار نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ اگر یہ احتمال ہے کہ وطی طلاق کے بعد کی گئی ہے تو یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ طلاق سے پہلے وطی کی گئی ہو ۔ پس رجعت میں شبہ ہو گیا اور شبہ اور شک کی وجہ سے رجعت ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے اس صورت میں رجعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔
اور اگر بچہ طلاق کے وقت سے دو سال سے زیادہ میں پیدا ہوا تو بلا شبہ رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں علوق یقیناً طلاق کے بعد ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اکثر مدت حمل دو سال ہے اور ظاہر حال یہی ہے کہ یہ علوق اس شخص سے ہوا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت کی طرف سے زنا منفی ہے۔ پس جب زمانہ عدت میں مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کی گئی ہے تو یہ شخص اس وطی کی وجہ سے مراجعت کرنے والا شمار ہوگا۔
Chapter on Establishing Lineage - The author of Hidayah explained the proof: When a child is born six months after marriage, necessarily the child is born less than six months from the time of divorce. And when the child is born less than six months from divorce, then conception occurred during marriage before divorce, and possibility of conception exists. Thus, if someone objects that this scenario is very far-fetched and rare, and it would be appropriate not to establish lineage, the answer is that in establishing lineage caution is observed. Therefore, by istihsan lineage is established. Some mashayikh said there is no need for this difficulty; the existence of the marital bed (firash) is sufficient for establishing lineage, and consideration of possibility of intercourse is not needed because marriage stands in place of intercourse. For example, if the spouses are a year's distance apart, then a child born in six months, lineage is established even if no intercourse or conception is imagined. However, some scholars refuted this view of the mashayikh, saying that for establishing lineage, conception must be conceivable and possible. That is why if a minor's wife gives birth, the child's lineage is not established from the minor. And the statement of some mashayikh that if the husband lives in the East and wife in the West with a year's distance, and she gives birth in six months, lineage is established from the Easterner, even though in this case conception is not conceivable or possible - the answer is that for the Easterner possibility of intercourse exists, in that the husband may be a saint and Allah can make a year's distance like a step, because the miracles of saints are true according to us. And the full mahr is obligatory upon the husband because when lineage is established from him, he becomes by Shari'ah the one who had intercourse, and since intercourse necessitates full mahr, in this case full mahr is obligatory. He said: The lineage of the child of a revocably divorced woman is established if she brings it within two years or more, as long as she does not admit the expiry of her iddah, due to the possibility of conception during the iddah, because she may have an extended period of purity. And if she brings it in less than two years, she becomes irrevocably separated from her husband due to the expiry of the iddah, and his lineage is established due to the existence of conception during marriage or during the iddah, and he does not become a revoker because conception is possible before divorce and after, so he does not become a revoker by doubt. And if she brings it in more than two years, it is a revocation because conception is after divorce, and apparently it is from him due to the exclusion of zina from her, so he becomes a revoker by intercourse. Translation: He said: The woman who is given revocable divorce - the lineage of her child is established provided she gives birth in two years or more, as long as the woman has not admitted the passing of her iddah, because there is possibility that the sperm was deposited during the iddah, since it is possible that this woman has an extended period of purity. And if this woman gives birth in less than two years, she becomes irrevocably separated from her husband due to the expiry of the iddah, and the child's lineage (from the husband) is established because conception occurred during marriage or during the iddah, and the husband will not be considered a revoker because conception is possible before divorce and after, so the husband by doubt will not be a revoker. And if this woman gives birth in more than two years, then revocation occurs because conception is after divorce, and it is apparent that the sperm is from this man because zina from the woman is negated, so he becomes a revoker by intercourse. Elaboration: The scenario is that a woman whom her husband gave revocable divorce gave birth at two years or more from the time of divorce, then lineage from the husband is established, provided the woman has not admitted the expiry of the iddah. The proof is that it is possible that this woman has an extended period of purity, and due to the prolongation of purity her iddah became long, and the husband had intercourse during the iddah, because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is lawful. So by this intercourse, revocation is also established and the child's lineage is also established. And if the child is born in less than two years, this woman becomes irrevocably separated from her husband, and the child's lineage is established from her husband. She becomes irrevocable because delivery causes irrevocable separation. And the reason for establishment of lineage is that if intercourse was done during marriage, then it is obvious, and if intercourse was done during the iddah, then also lineage is established because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is lawful in Shari'ah. But the husband will not be considered a revoker by this intercourse because if there is possibility that the intercourse was done after divorce, there is also possibility that it was done before divorce. So there is doubt in revocation, and revocation is not established by doubt. Therefore, in this case revocation is not established. And if the child is born more than two years from the time of divorce, then without doubt revocation is established because in this case conception is definitely after divorce, since the maximum period of pregnancy is two years, and the apparent situation is that this conception was from this man because zina from the woman is negated. So when intercourse occurred with the revocably divorced woman during the iddah period, this person is considered a revoker by this intercourse.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the Hanafi school on establishing lineage for the child of a revocably divorced woman (مطلقة رجعية). The text begins by discussing a preliminary proof: if a child is born six months after marriage, it necessarily means the child was conceived after marriage. The author then addresses an objection that this scenario might be rare, but the principle is that lineage is established with caution (احتياط), so by istihsan lineage is affirmed. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some mashayikh hold that the mere existence of the marital bed (فراش) is sufficient, without needing to conceive of actual intercourse. Others argue that conception must be possible; otherwise, as in the case of a minor or a distant husband, lineage is not established. The text supports the latter view, but also presents a miraculous exception for saints (اولیاء). Then the main ruling is given: for a revocably divorced woman, lineage is established if she gives birth within two years or more from the time of divorce, as long as she does not admit the expiry of her iddah. This is because the iddah may be prolonged if her menstrual cycle is extended, allowing the possibility of conception during the iddah. If she gives birth in less than two years, she becomes irrevocably divorced due to the expiry of the iddah, but lineage is still established because conception could have occurred during marriage or the iddah. However, in this case, the husband does not become a revoker because of doubt whether conception was before or after divorce. If she gives birth after two years, revocation is clearly established because conception must have occurred after divorce (since pregnancy can last up to two years). The text explains that intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is lawful and thus the child's lineage is from the husband. The commentary elaborates that in the case of less than two years, the woman becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) due to delivery, but lineage is still from the husband; the husband does not revoke because the timing of conception is uncertain. In the case of more than two years, revocation is certain because conception is after divorce.

Key Terms
علوق ('uluq): Conception; the embedding of the sperm in the womb resulting in pregnancy.
مطلقة رجعية (muṭallaqah rajʿiyyah): A woman who has been given a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) during her iddah, within which the husband may take her back without a new contract.
بائنہ (bā'inah): Irrevocably divorced; a woman who is no longer in iddah and cannot be taken back without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, if a revocably divorced woman gives birth two years and one day after the divorce, what is the ruling regarding lineage and revocation?
A) Lineage is not established, and revocation does not occur.
B) Lineage is established, and revocation does not occur because of doubt.
C) Lineage is established, and revocation occurs because conception is after divorce.
D) Lineage is established only if the woman admits iddah ended.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on lineage and revocation for a revocably divorced woman turns on the time between divorce and birth: birth within two years establishes lineage but not revocation; birth after two years establishes both.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Marital Bed vs. Possibility of Conception for Lineage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the sufficiency of firash

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions in the Hanafi dispute on whether the marital bed suffices for lineage or conception must be possible, and evaluate the proofs and the exception for saintly husbands.

Core Idea
The marital bed alone does not establish lineage; conception must be possible, except for saints where miracles make the impossible possible.

This lesson explores an important intra-madhhab debate within the Hanafi school: Does the mere existence of the marriage (firash) suffice to establish paternity, or must actual conception be conceivable? The text presents the views of some mashayikh who hold that firash alone is sufficient, and the preferred view that requires possibility of conception. A fascinating exception appears for saintly husbands. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's use of istihsan and the limits of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the first position
Some Hanafi mashayikh hold that the marital bed (firash) alone is sufficient for establishing lineage, without needing to verify the possibility of conception. They argue that marriage itself stands in place of intercourse.
They cite the case of distant spouses (one year apart) where lineage is still established.
2
State the second (preferred) position
The majority and the preferred view (mufta bihi) require that conception be possible. If it is impossible, lineage is not established. The case of a minor husband proves this: if a minor's wife gives birth, lineage is not established.
Also, the distant spouse scenario is explained using the possibility of saintly miracles.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the distant spouses example
The text concedes that for a saintly husband (wali), possibility exists through miracles (karamat al-awliya). For an ordinary husband, the distant scenario would not establish lineage. This preserves the principle that possibility is required.
The miracles of saints are accepted as true in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the istihsan argument for the original scenario
The author explains that even though the scenario of conception immediately after marriage is rare, lineage is established by istihsan (juristic preference) due to the principle of caution in lineage matters.
Istihsan overrides strict qiyas in this case.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if spouses are far apart (e.g., one year's travel) and the woman gives birth in six months, the first view would establish lineage, while the second view would not, unless the husband is a saint.
This difference has implications for paternity suits and inheritance.

صاحب ہدایہ نے اس دلیل کی وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ جب نکاح کے وقت سے چھ ماہ پر بچہ پیدا ہوا تو لازماً طلاق کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ کی ولادت ہوگی اور جب طلاق کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو گویا نکاح کی حالت میں طلاق سے پہلے علوق ہوا اور ولی علوق کا امکان بھی موجود ہے۔ اس طرح پر کہ اس عورت کے پیٹ پر لیٹ کر نکاح کیا اور لوگوں نے ان کے ایجاب و قبول کوسن بھی لیا اور نکاح ہو جانے پر انزال ہو کر نطفہ قرار پایا۔ اگر کوئی یہ اشکال کرے کہ یہ تصور بہت بعید اور امر نادر ہے تو مناسب یہ ہے کہ نسب ثابت نہ ہو تو جواب یہ ہو گا نسب ثابت کرنے میں احتیاط کی جاتی ہے۔ لہذا استحسانا نسب ثابت ہو جائیگا۔
اور بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ اس تکلیف کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔ نسب ثابت کرنے کیلئے فراش کا موجود ہونا کافی ہے اور امکان دخول کے اعتبار کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔ کیونکہ نکاح وطی کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے زوجین کے درمیان ایک سال کی مسافت ہے۔ پھر چھ ماہ میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو نسب ثابت ہو جائیگا ۔ اگر چہ دخول اور ولی کا وہم بھی نہیں ہے۔ مگر بعض حضرات نے مشائخ کے اس قول کو رد فرمایا ہے۔ انہوں نے فرمایا کہ ثبوت نسب کیلئے ولی کا متصور اور ممکن ہونا شرط ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر نابالغ کی بیوی سے بچہ پیدا ہوا ، تو اس بچہ کا نسب نابالغ سے ثابت نہیں ہوتا اور بعض مشائخ کا یہ کہنا کہ اگر شوہر مشرق میں رہتا ہے اور بیوی مغرب میں اور دونوں کے درمیان ایک سال کی مسافت ہے اور چھ ماہ میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو اس مشرقی سے بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ درانحالیکہ اس صورت میں ولی متصور اور ممکن نہیں تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مشرقی کے حق میں امکانِ وطی موجود ہے۔ بایں طور کہ شوہر ولی ہو اور اللہ تعالیٰ اس کے حق میں ایک سال کی مسافت کو ایک قدم کے برابر کر دے کیونکہ اولیاء کی کرامت ہمارے نزدیک برحق ہے۔ اولیاء کے بہت سے واقعات اس کی تائید میں موجود ہیں اور شوہر پر پورا مہر اسلئے واجب ہوگا کہ جب اس سے نسب ثابت ہو گیا تو گویا وہ بحکم شرع وطی کرنے والا ہوا اور چونکہ ولی کی وجہ سے پورا مہر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس صورت میں بھی پورا مہر واجب ہوگا۔
قال ويثبت نسب ولد المطلقة الرجعية اذا جاءت به لسنتين او اکثر مالم تقر بانقضاء عدتها لاحتمال العلوق فى حالة الجواز انها تكون ممتدة الطهر وان جاءت به لاقل من سنتين بالت من زوجها بانقضاء العدة وثبت نسبه لوجود العلوق فى النكاح اوفى العدة ولا يصير مراجعا لانه يحتمل العلوق قبل الطلاق ويحتمل بعده فلا يصير مراجعا بالشك وان جاءت به لاكثر من سنتين كانت رجعة لان العلوق بعد الطلاق والظاهر انه منه لانتقاء الزنا منها فيصير بالوطى مراجعا
ترجمہ فرمایا کہ جس عورت کو طلاق رجعی دی گئی ہے۔ اسکے بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ اس نے بچہ دو سال یا دو سال سے زیادہ میں جنا ہو جب تک کہ عورت نے اپنی عدت گذر جانے کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ احتمال ہے کہ عدت کی حالت میں نطفہ رہا ہو۔ اسلئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ یہ عورت ممتدۃ الطہر ہو اور اگر اس عورت نے دو سال سے کم میں بچہ جنا ہو تو وہ اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو گئی۔ عدت گذر جانے کی وجہ سے
اور بنچہ کا نسب (شوہر سے) ثابت ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ علوق (نطفہ ) نکاح میں پایا گیا یا عدت میں اور شوہر رجعت کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ علوق قبل الطلاق کا احتمال ہے اور بعد الطلاق کا بھی احتمال ہے۔ لہذا شوہر شک کی وجہ سے رجعت کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا اور اگر اس عورت نے دو سال سے زائد میں بچہ جنا تو رجعت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ علوق بعد الطلاق ہے اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ نطفہ اسی مرد سے ہو ۔ اسلئے کہ عورت سے زنا منتفی ہے۔ پس وہ ولی سے مراجعت کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت جس کو اس کے شوہر نے طلاق رجعی دی ہے۔ اسنے طلاق کے وقت سے دو سال پر یا دو سال سے زیادہ پر بچہ جنا تو شوہر سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ عورت نے عدت گذر جانے کا اقرار نہ کیا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہوسکتا ہے کہ یہ عورت ممتدۃ الطہر ہو اور طہر کے دراز ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کی عدت دراز ہوگئی ہو اور شوہر نے عدت کے زمانہ میں ولی کر لی ہو۔ کیونکہ معتدہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ ولی کرنا حلال ہے۔ پس اس وطی سے رجعت بھی ثابت ہوگی اور بچہ کا نسب بھی ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
اور اگر دو سال سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا ہے تو یہ عورت اپنے شوہر سے بائنہ ہو گئی اور اس بچہ کا نسب اس کے شوہر سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ بائنہ تو اسلئے ہو گئی کہ وضع حمل کی وجہ سے بائنہ ہو جاتی ہے۔
اور ثبوت نسب کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ولی حالت نکاح میں کی گئی ہے تب تو ظاہر ہے اور اگر عدت میں وطی کی گئی ہے تب بھی نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ معدہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کرنا شرعا حلال ہے۔ لیکن شوہر اس وطی سے مراجعت کرنے والا شمار نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ اگر یہ احتمال ہے کہ وطی طلاق کے بعد کی گئی ہے تو یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ طلاق سے پہلے وطی کی گئی ہو ۔ پس رجعت میں شبہ ہو گیا اور شبہ اور شک کی وجہ سے رجعت ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے اس صورت میں رجعت ثابت نہیں ہوگی۔
اور اگر بچہ طلاق کے وقت سے دو سال سے زیادہ میں پیدا ہوا تو بلا شبہ رجعت ثابت ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں علوق یقیناً طلاق کے بعد ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اکثر مدت حمل دو سال ہے اور ظاہر حال یہی ہے کہ یہ علوق اس شخص سے ہوا ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عورت کی طرف سے زنا منفی ہے۔ پس جب زمانہ عدت میں مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ وطی کی گئی ہے تو یہ شخص اس وطی کی وجہ سے مراجعت کرنے والا شمار ہوگا۔
Chapter on Establishing Lineage - The author of Hidayah explained the proof: When a child is born six months after marriage, necessarily the child is born less than six months from the time of divorce. And when the child is born less than six months from divorce, then conception occurred during marriage before divorce, and possibility of conception exists. Thus, if someone objects that this scenario is very far-fetched and rare, and it would be appropriate not to establish lineage, the answer is that in establishing lineage caution is observed. Therefore, by istihsan lineage is established. Some mashayikh said there is no need for this difficulty; the existence of the marital bed (firash) is sufficient for establishing lineage, and consideration of possibility of intercourse is not needed because marriage stands in place of intercourse. For example, if the spouses are a year's distance apart, then a child born in six months, lineage is established even if no intercourse or conception is imagined. However, some scholars refuted this view of the mashayikh, saying that for establishing lineage, conception must be conceivable and possible. That is why if a minor's wife gives birth, the child's lineage is not established from the minor. And the statement of some mashayikh that if the husband lives in the East and wife in the West with a year's distance, and she gives birth in six months, lineage is established from the Easterner, even though in this case conception is not conceivable or possible - the answer is that for the Easterner possibility of intercourse exists, in that the husband may be a saint and Allah can make a year's distance like a step, because the miracles of saints are true according to us. And the full mahr is obligatory upon the husband because when lineage is established from him, he becomes by Shari'ah the one who had intercourse, and since intercourse necessitates full mahr, in this case full mahr is obligatory. He said: The lineage of the child of a revocably divorced woman is established if she brings it within two years or more, as long as she does not admit the expiry of her iddah, due to the possibility of conception during the iddah, because she may have an extended period of purity. And if she brings it in less than two years, she becomes irrevocably separated from her husband due to the expiry of the iddah, and his lineage is established due to the existence of conception during marriage or during the iddah, and he does not become a revoker because conception is possible before divorce and after, so he does not become a revoker by doubt. And if she brings it in more than two years, it is a revocation because conception is after divorce, and apparently it is from him due to the exclusion of zina from her, so he becomes a revoker by intercourse. Translation: He said: The woman who is given revocable divorce - the lineage of her child is established provided she gives birth in two years or more, as long as the woman has not admitted the passing of her iddah, because there is possibility that the sperm was deposited during the iddah, since it is possible that this woman has an extended period of purity. And if this woman gives birth in less than two years, she becomes irrevocably separated from her husband due to the expiry of the iddah, and the child's lineage (from the husband) is established because conception occurred during marriage or during the iddah, and the husband will not be considered a revoker because conception is possible before divorce and after, so the husband by doubt will not be a revoker. And if this woman gives birth in more than two years, then revocation occurs because conception is after divorce, and it is apparent that the sperm is from this man because zina from the woman is negated, so he becomes a revoker by intercourse. Elaboration: The scenario is that a woman whom her husband gave revocable divorce gave birth at two years or more from the time of divorce, then lineage from the husband is established, provided the woman has not admitted the expiry of the iddah. The proof is that it is possible that this woman has an extended period of purity, and due to the prolongation of purity her iddah became long, and the husband had intercourse during the iddah, because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is lawful. So by this intercourse, revocation is also established and the child's lineage is also established. And if the child is born in less than two years, this woman becomes irrevocably separated from her husband, and the child's lineage is established from her husband. She becomes irrevocable because delivery causes irrevocable separation. And the reason for establishment of lineage is that if intercourse was done during marriage, then it is obvious, and if intercourse was done during the iddah, then also lineage is established because intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is lawful in Shari'ah. But the husband will not be considered a revoker by this intercourse because if there is possibility that the intercourse was done after divorce, there is also possibility that it was done before divorce. So there is doubt in revocation, and revocation is not established by doubt. Therefore, in this case revocation is not established. And if the child is born more than two years from the time of divorce, then without doubt revocation is established because in this case conception is definitely after divorce, since the maximum period of pregnancy is two years, and the apparent situation is that this conception was from this man because zina from the woman is negated. So when intercourse occurred with the revocably divorced woman during the iddah period, this person is considered a revoker by this intercourse.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof from the Hanafi school on establishing lineage for the child of a revocably divorced woman (مطلقة رجعية). The text begins by discussing a preliminary proof: if a child is born six months after marriage, it necessarily means the child was conceived after marriage. The author then addresses an objection that this scenario might be rare, but the principle is that lineage is established with caution (احتياط), so by istihsan lineage is affirmed. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some mashayikh hold that the mere existence of the marital bed (فراش) is sufficient, without needing to conceive of actual intercourse. Others argue that conception must be possible; otherwise, as in the case of a minor or a distant husband, lineage is not established. The text supports the latter view, but also presents a miraculous exception for saints (اولیاء). Then the main ruling is given: for a revocably divorced woman, lineage is established if she gives birth within two years or more from the time of divorce, as long as she does not admit the expiry of her iddah. This is because the iddah may be prolonged if her menstrual cycle is extended, allowing the possibility of conception during the iddah. If she gives birth in less than two years, she becomes irrevocably divorced due to the expiry of the iddah, but lineage is still established because conception could have occurred during marriage or the iddah. However, in this case, the husband does not become a revoker because of doubt whether conception was before or after divorce. If she gives birth after two years, revocation is clearly established because conception must have occurred after divorce (since pregnancy can last up to two years). The text explains that intercourse with a revocably divorced woman is lawful and thus the child's lineage is from the husband. The commentary elaborates that in the case of less than two years, the woman becomes bain (irrevocably divorced) due to delivery, but lineage is still from the husband; the husband does not revoke because the timing of conception is uncertain. In the case of more than two years, revocation is certain because conception is after divorce.

Key Terms
فراش (firāsh): The marital bed; by extension, the legal relationship of marriage that makes the husband's paternity presumptive.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning where a ruling is preferred due to necessity, custom, or equity over strict analogy.
کرامات الأولياء (karāmāt al-awliyā'): Miracles performed by Allah through His saintly servants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, why is lineage established in the distant spouse case (husband in East, wife in West, birth after six months)?
A) Because the marital bed alone is sufficient.
B) Because the husband may be a saint, making intercourse possible through a miracle.
C) Because the pregnancy is considered a miracle itself.
D) Because the woman's claim is accepted without proof.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's preferred view requires possibility of conception for lineage, but allows an exception for saints whose miracles can realize otherwise impossible scenarios.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Lineage of Child of Irrevocably Divorced Woman (Mubtūtah)
Ruling on lineage for child of irrevocably divorced woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the lineage of a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman is established in Hanafi law and apply the principle of precaution (iḥtiyāṭ) to similar cases.

Core Idea
Lineage is established if child born within two years, due to possible pre-divorce conception.

This passage addresses a nuanced scenario: a woman divorced irrevocably (talaq bain) gives birth. Since intercourse after such divorce is forbidden, one might assume the child cannot be from the former husband. However, Hanafi law upholds lineage under specific conditions, balancing the prohibition with the possibility of pre-existing pregnancy and the principle of precaution (iḥtiyāṭ). Let's examine the ruling and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is establishing lineage (nasab) for a child of an irrevocably divorced woman. The ruling states it is established if the child is born within two years of divorce; otherwise not, unless the husband claims paternity.
Note the two-year threshold—distinct from the usual iddah period.
2
Understand the reasoning (talīl)
The reason (ʿilla) is the possibility (iḥtimāl) that the child was conceived before divorce. Since the exact time of conception is unknown, and the marital bed (farāsh) may still have been intact at that time, lineage is affirmed out of caution.
This is an application of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqāṣidihā' indirectly through precaution.
3
Note the exception
If the child is born after two years, it is not attributed to the husband unless he explicitly claims paternity. The text also mentions a possibility of intercourse under doubt (shubhah) during ʿiddah, which could also establish lineage.
The husband's claim is an acceptance of responsibility.
4
Apply the principle of precaution
The principle of iḥtiyāṭ in lineage matters leans toward affirmation when there is any uncertainty, to avoid severing lineage without certainty.
This principle is also used in other areas like ḥudūd penalties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مبوتہ کے بچے کا نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے جبکہ وہ دو سال سے کم میں جنے
والمبتوته يثبت نسب ولدها اذا جاءت به لاقل من سنتين لانه يحتمل ان يكون الولد قائما وقت الطلاق فلايتيقن بزوال الفراش قبل العلوق فيثبت النسب احتياطاً واذا جاءت به لتمام سنتين من وقت الفرقة لم يثبت لان الحمل حادث بعد الطلاق فلايكون منه لان وطيها حرام الا ان يدعيه لانه التزمه وله وجه بان وطيها بشبهة في العدة
ترجمہ اور وہ عورت جس کو طلاق بائن دی گئی ہو اس کے بچہ کا نسب (شوہر سے) ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ جبکہ اس نے اس کو دو سال سے کم میں جنا۔ اسلئے کہ طلاق کے وقت بچہ کے موجود ہونے کا احتمال ہے۔ پس علوق سے پہلے فراش کے زائل ہونے کا یقین نہیں ہے۔ لہذا
The lineage of the child of an irrevocably divorced woman is established when she gives birth in less than two years. The Arabic text: And the irrevocably divorced woman, her child's lineage is established if she brings it in less than two years, because it is possible that the child was existing at the time of divorce, so the removal of the bed before conception is not certain, thus lineage is established as a precaution. And if she brings it after the completion of two years from the time of separation, it is not established because the pregnancy occurred after divorce, so it is not from him, for intercourse with her is forbidden, unless he claims it because he has undertaken it; and there is a possibility that he had intercourse with her under a dubious situation during the iddah. Translation: And the woman who has been given irrevocable divorce, the lineage of her child (from the husband) is established when she gives birth in less than two years, because there is possibility of the child's existence at the time of divorce. So before conception, the removal of the bed is not certain, therefore...
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for an irrevocably divorced woman (مبتوتہ). The key difference from the revocably divorced woman is that intercourse with her is forbidden after divorce (since iddah of bain does not allow intercourse). However, lineage is still established if the child is born within two years of divorce, because the child may have been conceived before divorce (i.e., the pregnancy existed at the time of divorce). The principle of caution (احتياط) is applied: since it is uncertain whether the marital bed ended before conception, lineage is affirmed. If the child is born after two years, lineage is not established because the pregnancy must have started after divorce, and since intercourse is haram, the child cannot be attributed to the husband unless he specifically claims paternity (يدعيه). The text also mentions an exception: if the husband had intercourse under a dubious situation (شبهة) during the iddah, there is a possibility the child is from him. The Urdu translation confirms the same: lineage is established if born in less than two years; otherwise not, unless the husband claims.

Key Terms
مبتوتہ (mubtūtah): A woman who has been given an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain), after which the husband cannot take her back except through a new marriage.
شبهة (shubhah): A dubious situation where intercourse may be considered excusable, possibly leading to lineage establishment.
احتياط (iḥtiyāṭ): Precaution; a principle of leaning towards affirming lineage when there is uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, if an irrevocably divorced woman gives birth 18 months after the divorce, what is the ruling on the child's lineage from the former husband?
A) Lineage is established because the child could have been conceived before divorce.
B) Lineage is not established because intercourse is haram.
C) Lineage is established only if the husband claims the child.
D) Lineage is not established because 18 months exceeds the maximum pregnancy period.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, lineage of a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman is established as a precaution within two years of divorce, reflecting the maxim that lineage is upheld when there is any possibility of conception within the marital bed.

Nikah — Marriage

Establishing Lineage for a Woman Divorced by Bayyin or Three Talaqs
Ruling on nasab for child born within two years after divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi two-year rule for lineage after irrevocable divorce and identify the exception when the husband claims paternity.

Core Idea
Within two years, lineage is established out of caution; beyond two years, only if the husband claims.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains how the Hanafi school determines the lineage of a child born after an irrevocable divorce. The key is the two-year maximum pregnancy duration and the principle of caution (ihtiyat). We will see how possibility and certainty govern the ruling, and when the husband's claim can override the time limit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
Establish the type of divorce (bayyin or three talaqs) and the key variable: the time between divorce and birth.
2
Apply the primary rule
If the child is born within two complete years from the time of separation, lineage is established automatically due to the possibility of conception before divorce.
This is based on ihtiyat to preserve lineage.
3
Apply the secondary rule
If the child is born exactly two years or more after the separation, lineage is not established because the pregnancy must have occurred after divorce, which is haram.
Certainty of post-divorce pregnancy blocks lineage.
4
Consider the exception
Even after two years, lineage can be established if the former husband voluntarily claims the child as his own.
The claim overrides the default rule due to the principle of ihtiyat and the possibility of intercourse during 'iddah in doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ثبوت النسب
احتیاطا نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
اور اگر اس عورت نے فرقت کے وقت سے پورے دو سال پر بچہ جنا تو نسب ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ حمل طلاق کے بعد پیدا ہوا ہے۔ تو اس مرد سے نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ (شوہر کا ) اس عورت کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حرام ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ اس کا مدعی ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس نے اس کا نسب اپنے ذمہ خود لازم کر لیا اور اس کی ایک وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اس سے عدت کے اندرشبہ میں ولی کی ہو۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی عورت کو ایک طلاق بائن یا تین طلاقیں دی گئی ہوں اور پھر فرقت کے وقت سے دو سال سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو اس بچہ کا نسب اس مطلقہ بائنہ کے شوہر سے ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ احتمال موجود ہے کہ طلاق کے وقت بچہ کا نطفہ قرار پا چکا ہو۔ پس اس امر کا یقین نہیں ہے کہ نطفہ قرار پانے سے پہلے عورت کا فراش صحیح ہونا زائل ہو گیا تھا۔ لہذا احتیاطاً نسب ثابت ہوگا۔
اور اگر فرقت کے وقت سے پورے دو سال پر بچہ پیدا ہوا تو نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں حمل بالیقین طلاق کے بعد پیدا ہوا ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اگر طلاق سے پہلے حدوث حمل تسلیم کیا جائے تو مدت حمل دو سال سے زیادہ ہو جائے گی ۔ حالانکہ یہ باطل ہے۔ پس جب حمل بعد الطلاق پیدا ہوا اور مرد کا مطلقہ بائنہ سے وطی کرنا حرام ہے۔ تو ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ عمل اس مرد کے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے اور جب حمل اس کے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے تو اس سے نسب بھی ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر یہ شخص اس کا مدعی ہو کہ ہی بچہ میرے ہی نطفہ سے ہے ،تو اس
سے نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ اگر چہ بچہ فرقت کے وقت سے دو سال سے زائد مدت میں پیدا ہوا ہو۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے اس بچہ کا نسب خود اپنے ذمہ لازم کر لیا ہے اور اس کی ایک شرعی توجیہ یہ بھی ہوسکتی ہے کہ اس شخص نے عادت کے زمانہ میں حلال سمجھ کر اس معندہ بائنہ کے ساتھ ولی کر لی ہو اور چونکہ ثبوت نسب میں احتیاط کی جاتی ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں بھی نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم
Chapter on Establishing Lineage. Out of caution, lineage will be established. And if that woman gave birth to a child at exactly two full years from the time of separation, then lineage will not be established. Because the pregnancy occurred after the divorce, so it will not be from that man, since (the husband's) intercourse with that woman is forbidden. Unless he claims it, because he has taken the lineage of the child upon himself voluntarily. And one reason for this is also that there may have been intercourse with her in doubt within the 'iddah. Explanation: If a woman was given one irrevocable divorce (talaq bain) or three divorces, and then she gives birth to a child within less than two years from the time of separation, the lineage of that child will be established from the husband of that irrevocably divorced woman. The proof is that there exists a possibility that at the time of divorce, the child's sperm had already been settled. So it is not certain that before the settling of the sperm, the woman's correct bed had been removed. Therefore, out of caution, lineage will be established. And if the child is born at exactly two full years from the time of separation, then lineage will not be established, because in this case, the pregnancy is certainly after the divorce. Because if we consider the occurrence of pregnancy before the divorce, then the duration of pregnancy would exceed two years, and this is invalid. So when the pregnancy occurred after the divorce and the man's intercourse with the irrevocably divorced woman is forbidden, then it is established that this act is not from that man's sperm, and when the pregnancy is not from his sperm, then lineage will not be established from him. Yes, if this person claims that this child is from my own sperm, then lineage will be established from him, even if the child is born after a period exceeding two years from the time of separation. The proof is that this person has taken the lineage of this child upon himself voluntarily, and one of its Shar'i justifications is that he may have committed intercourse with that irrevocably divorced woman considering it to be permissible during the time of the 'iddah, and since caution is applied in establishing lineage, in this case too lineage will be established. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on establishing lineage (nasab). The passage deals with a woman divorced by a bayyin (irrevocable) divorce or three talaqs. The key principle is that if a child is born within two years from the time of separation (firqat), lineage is established from the former husband due to the possibility that the child was conceived before the divorce. This is an application of the Hanafi principle of caution (ihtiyat) in lineage matters. The two-year maximum is based on the longest possible duration of pregnancy in the Hanafi school. If the child is born after exactly two full years, lineage is not established because the pregnancy must have occurred after the divorce, and intercourse with a bayyin divorced woman is haram. However, an exception is made if the former husband himself claims the child, as he voluntarily assumes responsibility. The reasoning includes that he might have mistaken the 'iddah period and had intercourse thinking it was halal. The passage follows the order: first states the ruling, then provides the proof based on possibility and certainty, then the exception for the claim.

Key Terms
ثبوت النسب (thubut al-nasab): Establishing the legal lineage of a child to a father.
فرقت (firqat): The time of separation; here it refers to the date of divorce.
مدعی (mudda'i): The person who claims something; here the husband who claims the child as his own.
احتیاط (ihtiyat): Legal caution; in lineage matters, the Hanafi school applies ihtiyat to preserve lineage when possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman is given three talaqs and gives birth exactly two years and one day after the divorce, what is the ruling on lineage according to this passage?
A) Lineage is established because it is within two years.
B) Lineage is established only if the husband claims paternity.
C) Lineage is not established even if the husband claims.
D) Lineage is not established because it is beyond two years, unless the husband claims.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes lineage within two years of irrevocable divorce out of caution; after two years, lineage requires the husband's claim.
