Lineage for a Minor Divorced Woman: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage time for a minor divorcée

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf on the maximum time for establishing lineage from a minor divorced irrevocably, and explain the proof (dalil) for each position.

Core Idea
Shari'ah's ruling on 'iddah completion overrides personal admission; thus for a minor bayyin divorce, lineage is only within 9 months.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the lineage (nasab) of a child born to a minor woman (saghira yujama' mithluha) after an irrevocable divorce. The dispute centers on how Shari'ah determines the end of 'iddah and whether the woman's own admission can extend the period for paternity. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your skill in weighing conflicting proofs within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the passage addresses a specific case: a minor girl who is divorced irrevocably (bayyin) and later gives birth. The key question is within what maximum time from the divorce can the child be attributed to the ex-husband.
The woman is 'saghira yujama' mithluha' — a minor but physically mature enough for intercourse.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that lineage is only established if the child is born within nine months of the divorce (specifically, less than nine months). Abu Yusuf holds that for a bayyin divorce, lineage can be established up to two years; for a raj'i divorce, up to twenty-seven months.
The difference turns on whether the completion of 'iddah is determined by the Shari'ah (three months) or by the woman's own admission of not having menstruated.
3
Analyze the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
They cite Quran 65:4 which sets the 'iddah of a minor who does not menstruate as three months. Once those months pass, the Shari'ah definitively declares the 'iddah complete. This legal presumption is stronger than any admission by the woman because the Shari'ah does not admit of falsehood.
Their proof is based on the third argument (dalil thālith) that Shari'ah's ruling is above the woman's admission.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that since the woman has not admitted to the completion of her 'iddah, she remains in a state where pregnancy is possible. He analogizes her to an adult woman in 'iddah, for whom lineage can be established up to two years of maximum pregnancy. For raj'i divorce, he adds the three months of 'iddah during which intercourse is allowed, totaling twenty-seven months.
Abu Yusuf's proof relies on the possibility (iḥtimāl) of pregnancy without her admission, but the majority considers the Shari'ah's ruling as overriding that possibility.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preponderance)
The text indicates that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) because their proof is based on a clear Quranic text and the principle that Shari'ah's ruling is immune to falsehood, whereas the woman's admission can be mistaken or false.
Thus, for fatwa, the operative ruling is that for a minor divorced irrevocably, lineage is only within nine months; for raj'i, also within nine months (since 'iddah is three months and the possibility of later intercourse is not considered).

گزرنے کا اقرار کر لیتی اور اس کے بعد چھ ماہ پر بچہ پیدا ہوتا تو نسب ثابت نہیں ہوتا۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ اگر مراہقہ نے طلاق کے وقت سے نو ماہ پر بچہ جنا تو اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر وہ صغیرہ مطلقہ رجعیہ ہوتو طرفین کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے۔ یعنی اگر طلاق کے وقت سے نو ماہ سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ ورنہ نہیں اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک ستائیس ماہ تک نسب ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ چونکہ مطلقہ رجعیہ کے ساتھ عدت کے زمانہ میں وطی کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسلئے ممکن ہے کہ عدت کے آخری وقت میں ولی کی ہو اور پھر اکثر مدت حمل میں بچہ کی ولادت ہوئی ہو۔ تو اس طرح ستائیس ماہ ہو جائیں گے ۔ تین ماہ عدت کے اور چوٹیں ماه اکثر مدت حمل کے۔ لہذا اگر طلاق کے وقت سے ستائیس ماہ پر بچہ پیدا ہوا تو اس کا نسب ثابت ہوگا اور اگر صغیرہ نے عدت کے زمانے
When this [woman] is a minor (saghira) with whom intercourse can take place, she gives birth at nine months, then the lineage of that child will not be established until she gives birth in less than nine months. Sayings of the jurists: If the irrevocably divorced woman is a minor with whom intercourse can take place, and she brings a child at nine months, it does not become obligatory (upon him) until she brings it at less than nine months, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And Abu Yusuf said: Lineage is established from him up to two years, because she is in 'iddah, it is possible that she is pregnant, and she has not admitted to the completion of 'iddah, so she becomes like an adult woman. And their (the two's) proof is that the completion of her 'iddah has a specific time, which is three months. So with the passage of that time, the Shari'ah gives the ruling of completion, and this is stronger in indication than her admission, because it does not admit of disagreement, while her admission does admit of disagreement. And if she is divorced by a raj'i divorce, the answer is the same according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And according to him (Abu Yusuf), it is established up to twenty-seven months, because he considers that intercourse occurred at the end of the 'iddah, which is three months, and then she brings the child at the maximum duration of pregnancy, which is two years. And if the minor claimed pregnancy during the 'iddah, then the answer in her case and in the case of an adult is the same, because by her admission, the ruling of her reaching adulthood is given. Translation: So if the irrevocably divorced woman is a minor with whom intercourse can take place, then she gives birth at nine months (from the time of divorce), then the lineage will not become obligatory upon the man, until (if) she gives birth in less than nine months (then lineage is established). This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. And Imam Abu Yusuf said that lineage will be established from him up to two years. Abu Yusuf's proof is that this woman in 'iddah has the possibility of being pregnant, and she has not admitted to the completion of 'iddah, so she becomes similar to an adult woman. And the two's proof is that the completion of this woman's 'iddah has a specific time, and that is the months of 'iddah. So with their passage, the Shari'ah gives the ruling of completion of her 'iddah, and this is stronger than her admission, because the Shari'ah ruling does not admit of disagreement, while her admission does admit of it. And if this minor is given a raj'i divorce, then according to the two, the same ruling applies. And according to Abu Yusuf, lineage will be established up to twenty-seven months. Because since intercourse is permissible with a raj'i divorcée during the period of 'iddah, it is possible that intercourse occurred at the end of the 'iddah, and then the child was born at the maximum duration of pregnancy. In this way, it becomes twenty-seven months: three months of 'iddah and twenty-four months of maximum pregnancy. Therefore, if the child is born at twenty-seven months from the time of divorce, his lineage will be established. And if the minor claimed to be pregnant during the 'iddah period...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue: a minor girl (who can be sexually active) is divorced irrevocably (bayyin) and gives birth at nine months from the time of divorce. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, lineage is not established unless she gives birth in less than nine months. Their reasoning: the 'iddah of a minor who does not menstruate is three months (Quran 65:4). Once those months pass, Shari'ah declares her 'iddah complete, regardless of her own admission. This legal presumption is stronger than her potential claim because the Shari'ah's ruling does not admit of falsehood. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: since she is in 'iddah and has not admitted to its completion, there remains a possibility she is pregnant. Therefore, like an adult woman in 'iddah, lineage is possible up to two years (maximum pregnancy duration). For a raj'i divorce, the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain the same rule (three months 'iddah). Abu Yusuf extends it to 27 months because in raj'i divorce, intercourse is allowed during 'iddah, so he presumes intercourse at the end of the three-month 'iddah, adding 24 months (max pregnancy), totaling 27 months. If the minor claims pregnancy during 'iddah, both sides agree the ruling is same as an adult because her claim implies she has reached adulthood (since only an adult can be pregnant). The passage presents Abu Yusuf's proof first, then the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), followed by practical consequences.

Key Terms
صغیرہ (saghira): A minor girl who has not reached puberty but is capable of sexual intercourse (yujama' mithluha).
مراہقہ (murahiqa): A girl approaching puberty; in the text it is used interchangeably with saghira but specifically for a minor who is close to menstruation.
مدخول بہا (madkhul biha): A woman with whom the husband has consummated marriage.
اقرار (iqrar): Admission or confession; here the woman's admission that her 'iddah has ended.
عدد ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what is the maximum time within which a minor (saghira yujama' mithluha) divorced irrevocably can give birth for lineage to be established from the former husband?
A) Two years from divorce
B) Twenty-seven months from divorce
C) Nine months from divorce (less than nine months)
D) Six months from divorce

Key Takeaway
For a minor divorced irrevocably, the relied-upon Hanafi view restricts lineage to nine months from divorce, based on the Quranic 'iddah of three months.
